جو رشتے نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں وہ رضاعت سے بھی حرام ہوتے ہیں
قال ويحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب للحديث الذى روينا الاام اخته من الرضاع فانه يجوزان يتزوجها ولايجوزان يتزوج ام اخته من النسب لانها تكون امه او موطوة ابيه بخلاف الرضاع ترجمه قدوری نے کہا کہ رضاعت سے وہ تمام رشتے حرام ہو جاتے ہیں جو نسب سے حرام ہوتے ہیں ، اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ،مگر اس کی رضاعی بہن کی ماں۔ اسلئے کہ جائز ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ نکاح کرے اور نہیں جائز ہے یہ کہ نکاح کرے اپنی نسبی بہن کی ماں سے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ماں ہوگی یا اس کے باپ کی موطوہ بخلاف رضاعت کے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے اس عبارت میں ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ جو عورتیں نسب کی وجہ سے حرام ہیں وہ تمام عورتیں رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی حرام ہوں گی۔ دلیل میں وہ حدیث بیان کی ہے جو اوائل کتاب النکاح میں گذر چکی ۔ لیکن اس ضابطہ سے دو صورتوں کا استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ یعنی دو صورتیں ایسی ہیں کہ جہاں رضاعت کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ لیکن نسب کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ پہلی صورت الا ام اخته من الرضاع سے ذکر فرمائی لیکن یہ عبارت تین صورتوں کو شامل ہے کیونکہ من الرضاع کا تعلق اخت اور ام دونوں سے ہوگا۔ یا صرف اخت سے یا صرف ام سے۔ پہلی صورت میں مطلب ہوگا کہ رضاعی بہن کی رضاعی ماں سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ خالد اور زینب دونوں نے ہندہ کا دودھ پیا اور فقط زینب نے ام سلمہ کا دودھ پیا تو اب خالد کا نکاح ام سلمہ سے جائز ہے حالانکہ ام سلمہ خالد کی رضاعی بہن زینب کی رضاعی ماں ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ رضاعی بہن کی نسبی ماں سے نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ زید اور ساجدہ نے ایک اجنبی عورت کا دودھ پیا۔ مگر زید نے ساجدہ کی نسبی ماں کا دودھ نہیں پیا تو زید کیلئے اس کی رضاعی بہن ساجدہ کی نبی ماں حلال ہے۔ اور تیسری صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ نبی بہن کی رضاعی ماں کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ زید کی نسبی بہن ہے اور بہن کی رضاعی ماں ہے جس نے زید کو دودھ نہیں پلایا ہے تو اس نسبی بہن کی رضاعی ماں سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔
البتہ اپنی نسبی بہن کی نسیمی ماں سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نبی بہن کی نبی ماں یا تو اس کی بھی ماں ہوگی اگر دونوں حقیقی بھائی بہن ہیں اور یا اسکے باپ کی موطوہ ہوگی اور اگر دونوں کا باپ ایک ہے اور ماں الگ الگ ہے۔ اور ان دونوں صورتوں (ماں اور باپ کی موطوۃ ) میں نکاح ناجائز ہے۔ اسلئے اس نسبی رشتہ کی صورت میں نکاح ناجائز قرادیا گیا اور رضاعت کی صورت میں ان میں سے کوئی قباحت نہیں۔ اسلئے رضاعت کی صورت میں نکاح جائز رکھا گیا ہے۔
The relationships that are prohibited by lineage are also prohibited by fosterage. He said: And what is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by fosterage, due to the hadith we narrated, except the mother of his foster sister, for it is permissible for him to marry her, and it is not permissible for him to marry the mother of his biological sister, because she would be his mother or the one slept with by his father, unlike fosterage. Translation: Quduri said: All relationships that are prohibited by lineage become prohibited by fosterage, due to the hadith we narrated, except the mother of his foster sister. Because it is permissible for him to marry her, and it is not permissible for him to marry the mother of his biological sister, because she would be his mother or the one slept with by his father, contrary to fosterage. Explanation: The author Quduri has stated a principle in this expression: that all women who are prohibited by lineage are also prohibited by fosterage. The evidence is the hadith that passed earlier in the beginning of the Book of Nikah. But he made an exception of two situations. That is, there are two situations where prohibition is not established by fosterage, but is established by lineage. The first exception is mentioned as 'except the mother of his foster sister.' But this phrase covers three possibilities because 'min al-rada'' can attach to both 'sister' and 'mother'. First possibility: it means marrying the foster mother of one's foster sister is permissible. Example: Khalid and Zaynab both drank the milk of Hind, and only Zaynab drank the milk of Umm Salama. Then Khalid's marriage to Umm Salama is permissible, even though Umm Salama is the foster mother of Khalid's foster sister Zaynab. Second possibility: it means marrying the biological mother of one's foster sister is permissible. Example: Zayd and Sajida both drank the milk of a stranger woman, but Zayd did not drink the milk of Sajida's biological mother. Then for Zayd, the biological mother of his foster sister Sajida is permissible. Third possibility: it means marrying the foster mother of one's biological sister is permissible. Example: Zayd has a biological sister, and the sister's foster mother is someone who did not nurse Zayd. So he can marry the foster mother of his biological sister. However, marrying the biological mother of one's biological sister is not permissible. Because the biological mother of the biological sister is either also his mother (if they are full siblings) or the one slept with by his father (if they are paternal half-siblings). In both cases (mother and father's consort), marriage is prohibited. Therefore, this lineage-based relationship is prohibited, while in the fosterage case there is no such problem. Hence, in the fosterage case, marriage is permitted.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents a core principle of Hanafi fiqh: fosterage (rada') creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage (nasab), based on the well-known hadith. However, there is an exception: the mother of one's foster sister is not prohibited. The commentator explains that Quduri's phrase 'except the mother of his foster sister' (الا ام اخته من الرضاع) is ambiguous and can be interpreted in three ways, all of which are permissible. The three scenarios are: (1) A man may marry the foster mother of his foster sister (i.e., the woman who nursed his foster sister, but not him). (2) A man may marry the biological mother of his foster sister (i.e., the woman who gave birth to his foster sister but did not nurse him). (3) A man may marry the foster mother of his biological sister (i.e., the woman who nursed his biological sister but not him). In all these cases, there is no prohibition because the link is through fosterage, not lineage. In contrast, the biological mother of one's biological sister is either one's own mother (if full sibling) or one's father's wife (if paternal half-sibling), both of whom are permanently prohibited. The passage thus clarifies that the general rule has specific limits, and students must understand the nuanced application of the principle.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Biological lineage or blood relationship.
رضاعی بہن (rada'i bahan): Foster sister: a female who was nursed by the same woman that nursed the man, making them siblings by fosterage.
موطوہ (mawtuw'ah): A woman with whom a man has had sexual intercourse; here refers to the father's wife (stepmother) who is prohibited forever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following marriages is permissible according to the Hanafi school based on this passage?
A) Marrying one's biological sister's biological mother.
B) Marrying one's foster sister's foster mother.
C) Marrying one's biological sister's foster mother.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The mother of one's foster sister is not prohibited, unlike the biological case, because the foster link does not extend to the mother's own relations.

Marrying the Sister of a Foster Son: The Hanafi Exception
States the permissibility of marrying the sister of one's foster son and explains the rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying the sister of a foster son and explain the Hanafi rationale distinguishing fosterage from lineage.

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibits only the foster child, not their siblings; lineage prohibition extends to siblings because of the mother's relationship.

In this passage, the author explains a key exception to the principle that fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage. While it is haram to marry the sister of one's biological son, it is halal to marry the sister of one's foster son. The difference lies in the underlying cause (illah): sexual relations with the mother. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying the sister of one's foster son. Three forms are considered: the foster son's foster sister, the foster son's biological sister, and the biological son's foster sister. All three are declared permissible (mubah).
The ruling is an exception to the general rule that fosterage mirrors lineage.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is aqli (reasoning). The text states: 'because when he had intercourse with her mother, she became prohibited to him.' This cause exists in lineage but is absent in fosterage.
The dalil is not a transmitted text but a rational comparison.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illah) for prohibition in lineage is the man's sexual intercourse with the mother. Since in fosterage the man has no such relationship with the foster mother, the cause is absent, and therefore the sister of the foster son remains permissible.
This is a clear example of ta'lil (reason-based derivation).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school generally extends fosterage prohibitions to siblings and their descendants, so they would prohibit marrying the sister of a foster son. The Hanafi school restricts it to the direct foster child.
The difference stems from interpreting the scope of 'yahrumu min al-rada'i ma yahrumu min al-nasab'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a Hanafi may marry the sister of his foster son, while a Shafi'i may not. This affects actual marriage contracts and family relations.
The practical difference is the bottom line for fiqh application.

Source Text

Marrying the sister of one's foster son is permissible. And it is permissible to marry the sister of his foster son, and that is not permissible from lineage because when he had intercourse with her mother, she became prohibited to him, and this meaning does not exist in fosterage. Translation: And it is permissible to marry the sister of one's foster son. And this is not permissible from lineage because when he had intercourse with her mother, she (the mother) became prohibited to him, and this meaning does not exist in fosterage. Explanation: The second exception from the mentioned principle is being mentioned by the author (may Allah have mercy on him). In this second case, there are three possibilities: (1) The foster son's foster sister, (2) The foster son's biological sister, (3) The biological son's foster sister. In all these possibilities, marriage is valid. By analogy with the mentioned examples, deriving their examples is not difficult. Commentary
This passage presents a second exception to the general rule that fosterage mirrors lineage. It is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster son, whether that sister is a foster sister of the son (i.e., nursed by the same woman), a biological sister of the foster son, or a foster sister of the biological son. The underlying reason is that the prohibition that exists for a biological son's sister is based on the fact that the man has had sexual relations with the mother (either because she is his wife or his father's wife). Since fosterage does not create this kind of relationship with the mother (the foster mother is not necessarily sexually related to him), the sister of the foster son is not prohibited. In contrast, the biological son's biological sister is prohibited because the son's mother is either the man's wife or his father's wife, making him prohibited to marry any daughter from that woman. The passage ends abruptly, but the point is clear: the exception applies to the sister of the foster son in all three forms, while the biological son's biological sister remains prohibited.

Key Terms
رضاعی بیٹا (rada'i beta): Foster son: a male child who was nursed by a woman, making him her foster son and creating prohibitions between him and the woman's family.
اخت ابنه من الرضاع (ukht ibnihi min al-rada'): The sister of his foster son, which can be a foster sister (nursed by same woman), biological sister, or a foster sister of his biological son.

Exception: Mother of Foster Sister from Fosterage Does Not Prohibit Marriage
Explaining an exception to the rule of prohibition through fosterage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule of fosterage prohibitions and identify the three permissible marriage scenarios derived from the phrase 'except the mother of his sister from fosterage.'

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits, but indirect links like a foster sister's mother are permissible.

This passage from Ashraf al-Bidaya unpacks a critical exception to the well-known rule that fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as lineage. While the hadith 'whatever is forbidden due to lineage is forbidden due to fosterage' is clear, there are subtle cases where a fosterage relationship does not trigger prohibition. The commentary dives into the ambiguous phrase 'except the mother of his sister from fosterage,' revealing three distinct scenarios where marriage is actually permissible.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the rule: All women prohibited by lineage are prohibited by fosterage.
This rule is from al-Quduri's matn and based on a hadith.
2
Locate the exception phrase
Find the phrase 'except the mother of his sister from fosterage' (الا ام اخته من الرضاع).
The word 'from fosterage' (من الرضاع) creates grammatical ambiguity.
3
Parse the grammatical ambiguity
Determine the three possible attachments of 'from fosterage': to both 'sister' and 'mother', to 'sister' only, or to 'mother' only.
Each attachment yields a different permissible marriage scenario.
4
Apply each interpretation
Work through the examples: (1) foster mother of foster sister, (2) lineage mother of foster sister, (3) foster mother of lineage sister.
In each case, the man did not nurse from the woman in question.
5
Distinguish the lineage case
Understand why the lineage mother of one's lineage sister remains prohibited: she is either one's own mother or father's wife.
The prohibition is based on lineage, not fosterage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الرضاع
. اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم بہن کی ماں سے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ماں ہوگی یا اس کے باپ کی موطوہ بخلاف رضاعت کے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے اس عبارت میں ایک ضابطہ بیان فرمایا ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ جو عورتیں نسب کی وجہ سے حرام ہیں وہ تمام عورتیں رضاعت کی وجہ سے بھی حرام ہوں گی۔ دلیل میں وہ حدیث بیان کی ہے جو اوائل کتاب النکاح میں گذر چکی ۔ لیکن اس ضابطہ سے دو صورتوں کا استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ یعنی دو صورتیں ایسی ہیں کہ جہاں رضاعت کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ لیکن نسب کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ پہلی صورت الا ام اخته من الرضاع سے ذکر فرمائی لیکن یہ عبارت تین صورتوں کو شامل ہے کیونکہ من الرضاع کا تعلق اخت اور ام دونوں سے ہوگا۔ یا صرف اخت سے یا صرف ام سے۔ پہلی صورت میں مطلب ہوگا کہ رضاعی بہن کی رضاعی ماں سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ خالد اور زینب دونوں نے ہندہ کا دودھ پیا اور فقط زینب نے ام سلمہ کا دودھ پیا تو اب خالد کا نکاح ام سلمہ سے جائز ہے حالانکہ ام سلمہ خالد کی رضاعی بہن زینب کی رضاعی ماں ہے اور دوسری صورت میں مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ رضاعی بہن کی نسبی ماں سے نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ زید اور ساجدہ نے ایک اجنبی عورت کا دودھ پیا۔ مگر زید نے ساجدہ کی نسبی ماں کا دودھ نہیں پیا تو زید کیلئے اس کی رضاعی بہن ساجدہ کی نبی ماں حلال ہے۔ اور تیسری صورت میں مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ نبی بہن کی رضاعی ماں کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ زید کی نسبی بہن ہے اور بہن کی رضاعی ماں ہے جس نے زید کو دودھ نہیں پلایا ہے تو اس نسبی بہن کی رضاعی ماں سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔
البتہ اپنی نسبی بہن کی نسیمی ماں سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نبی بہن کی نبی ماں یا تو اس کی بھی ماں ہوگی اگر دونوں حقیقی بھائی بہن ہیں اور یا اسکے باپ کی موطوہ ہوگی اور اگر دونوں کا باپ ایک ہے اور ماں الگ الگ ہے۔ اور ان دونوں صورتوں (ماں اور باپ کی موطوۃ ) میں نکاح ناجائز ہے۔ اسلئے اس نسبی رشتہ کی صورت میں نکاح ناجائز قرادیا گیا اور رضاعت کی صورت میں ان میں سے کوئی قباحت نہیں۔ اسلئے رضاعت کی صورت میں نکاح جائز رکھا گیا ہے۔
Book of Fosterage. Ashraf al-Bidaya commentary on Hidaya volume four. (Concerning) the sister's mother. Because she would be his mother or his father's wife, unlike in fosterage. Explanation: Sahib Quduri stated a rule in this phrase: That whatever women are prohibited due to lineage are all prohibited due to fosterage as well. The proof is the hadith mentioned earlier in the Book of Marriage. However, he made two exceptions to this rule: there are two cases where prohibition is not established due to fosterage but is established due to lineage. The first case is mentioned from 'except the mother of his sister from fosterage.' But this phrase includes three possibilities because 'from fosterage' can relate to both 'sister' and 'mother,' or only to 'sister,' or only to 'mother.' In the first possibility, the meaning is that marriage to the foster mother of one's foster sister is permissible. The example: Khalid and Zainab both drank the milk of Hind, but only Zainab drank the milk of Umm Salma. So marriage of Khalid to Umm Salma is permissible, even though Umm Salma is the foster mother of Khalid's foster sister Zainab. In the second possibility, the meaning is that marriage to the lineage mother of one's foster sister is permissible. The example: Zaid and Sajida drank the milk of a stranger woman, but Zaid did not drink the milk of Sajida's lineage mother. So for Zaid, the lineage mother of his foster sister Sajida is permissible. In the third possibility, the meaning is that marriage to the foster mother of one's lineage sister is permissible. The example: Zaid has a lineage sister, and that sister has a foster mother who did not nurse Zaid. So he may marry the foster mother of his lineage sister. However, marriage to the lineage mother of one's lineage sister is not permissible. Because the lineage mother of his lineage sister is either his own mother (if they are full siblings) or his father's wife (if they share father but different mothers). In both cases (mother or father's wife), marriage is forbidden. Therefore, in the lineage relationship, marriage was declared forbidden, and in the fosterage relationship, none of these objections exist, so marriage was made permissible.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Bidaya explains an exception to the well-known rule that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as lineage. The author first states the general rule from al-Quduri: all women prohibited by lineage are prohibited by fosterage. Then he notes two exceptions, but the first exception, 'except the mother of his sister from fosterage,' is ambiguous in Arabic grammar, allowing three interpretations. The commentary carefully unpacks each: (1) marriage to the foster mother of one's foster sister is permissible, (2) marriage to the lineage mother of one's foster sister is permissible, and (3) marriage to the foster mother of one's lineage sister is permissible. In each case, the fosterage link does not create a direct maternal relationship. However, if a woman is one's own lineage mother or father's wife, she is absolutely forbidden. The key point: fosterage creates prohibition only for relationships directly analogous to lineage—a woman is forbidden if she would have been forbidden had the fosterage been lineage, but not if the connection is indirect, as in these examples.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage: the relationship created by a woman nursing a child, establishing certain marriage prohibitions.
استثناء (istithna'): An exception to a general rule; here, the two cases where fosterage does not create prohibition despite lineage relationships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fosterage creates prohibitions analogous to lineage, but indirect links (e.g., a foster sister's mother who did not nurse the man) do not trigger prohibition, allowing marriage in three specific scenarios.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Marriage to Sister of Foster Son is Permissible
Stating ruling with reason and expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of a foster son and distinguish it from the lineage case using the legal reasoning (ʿilla).

Core Idea
A foster son's sister is permissible to marry because the prohibition's cause—intercourse with her mother—is absent in fosterage.

In this lesson, we examine a specific exception to the general rule that fosterage mirrors lineage in marriage prohibitions. The text from al-Hidayah declares it permissible to marry the sister of one's foster son, whereas in lineage such a marriage is forbidden. Understanding the underlying reasoning (ʿilla) will help you apply the correct ruling in related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the explicit statement that marrying the sister of a foster son is permissible. Note that the author contrasts it with the lineage case where it is not permissible.
2
Understand the reasoning for lineage prohibition
The text states that in lineage, the sister becomes prohibited because the father has had intercourse with her mother. This maternal relation (being a stepdaughter or daughter) creates a prohibition.
This reason is specific to lineage because the father's intercourse with the mother directly establishes a mahram relationship.
3
Recognize the absence of that reasoning in fosterage
In fosterage, the foster son is not a biological child, and the foster father has no marital relationship with the foster son's mother. Therefore, the cause for prohibition does not exist.
Fosterage only creates prohibitions between the foster parent and the foster child, not with the child's relatives.
4
Apply to the three scenarios
The commentary lists three possibilities: (1) foster sister of foster son, (2) lineage sister of foster son, (3) foster sister of lineage son. In all three, marriage is permissible because the prohibition cause is absent.
Only the lineage sister of one's lineage son is prohibited, which is the normal case.
5
Contrast with the lineage sister of one's lineage son
If the sister is a full biological sister of one's own biological son (i.e., one's daughter) or a stepdaughter through marriage to the mother, then marriage is prohibited due to the existing mahram relationship.
This distinction is crucial for correct fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن سے نکاح جائز ہے
و يجوز تزوج اخت ابنه من الرضاع ولا يجوز ذلك من النسب لانه لما وطى امها حرمت اليه ولم يوجد هذا المعنى في الرضاع
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے اپنے رضاعی بیٹے کی بہن سے نکاح کرنا۔ اور یہ نسب سے جائز نہیں کیونکہ جب اس کی ماں سے وطی کی تو (ماں) اس پر حرام ہو گئی اور یہ معنی رضاعت میں موجود نہیں ہیں۔ تشریح دوسری صورت جس کا مذکورہ ضابطہ سے استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ مصنف علیہ الرحمۃ اس کو ذکر فرمارہے ہیں ۔ اس دوسری صورت میں بھی تین احتمال ہیں۔ (1) رضاعی بیٹے کی رضاعی بہن (2) رضاعی بیٹے کی نسبی بہن (3) نسبی بیٹے کی رضاعی بہن۔ ان متنوع احتمالات میں نکاح درست ہے مذکورہ امثلہ پر قیاس کر کے ان کی مثالوں کو نکالنا دشوار نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر ان دونوں میں نسبی رشتہ ہے یعنی نسبی بیٹے کی نسبی بہن ہے تو اس نسبی بیٹے کی نسبی بہن سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس کے نسبی بیٹے کی بہن اگر اسی کے نطفہ سے ہے تو وہ اس کی بیٹی ہوگی ۔ اور اگر اس کے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے اور اس کے بیٹے کی صرف ماں شریک بہن ہے تو یہ رہیہ ہوگی۔ اور رہیہ کی ماں کے ساتھ اگر دخول کر لیا جائے تو رہیہ حرام ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے بیان فرمایا کہ جب بیٹے کی بہن کی ماں کے ساتھ وطی کر چکا تو وہ بہن اس باپ پر حرام ہو گئی۔ بہر حال کچھ بھی ہو دونوں صورتوں (بیٹی ہو یا رہیہ ) میں اس نسبی بیٹے کی نسبی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور رضاعت میں ان دونوں وجہوں میں سے کوئی موجود نہیں اسلئے رضاعت کی صورت میں نکاح جائز قرار دیا گیا۔
Marriage to the sister of one's foster son is permissible. 'And it is permissible to marry the sister of his son from fosterage, and it is not permissible from lineage because when he had intercourse with her mother, she became prohibited to him, and this meaning is not present in fosterage.' Translation: And it is permissible to marry the sister of one's foster son. And this is not permissible from lineage because when he had intercourse with her mother, (the mother) became prohibited to him, and this meaning is not present in fosterage. Explanation: The second case that is excepted from the aforementioned rule. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) is mentioning it. In this second case, there are also three possibilities: (1) the foster sister of one's foster son, (2) the lineage sister of one's foster son, (3) the foster sister of one's lineage son. Marriage in these various possibilities is valid; by analogizing to the mentioned examples, it is not difficult to derive their examples. But if there is a lineage relationship between them, i.e., the lineage sister of one's lineage son, then marrying the lineage sister of that lineage son is not permissible. The reason: if his lineage son's sister is from his own sperm, then she is his daughter. And if she is not from his sperm and she is only a half-sister sharing the mother with his son, then she is a stepdaughter (rabibah). And if intercourse has occurred with the stepdaughter's mother, then the stepdaughter becomes prohibited to him. The author of al-Hidayah stated: when he has had intercourse with the mother of his son's sister, that sister becomes prohibited to the father. In any case, in both situations (she is a daughter or a stepdaughter), marriage to the lineage sister of his lineage son is not permissible. And in fosterage, neither of these two reasons exists, so in the case of fosterage, marriage was declared permissible.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the second exception to the general rule that fosterage mirrors lineage in prohibition. The base text from al-Hidayah states that it is permissible to marry the sister of one's foster son, whereas it is not permissible in lineage because of the relationship with the mother. The commentary explains that this second exception also includes three possibilities: (1) the foster sister of one's foster son, (2) the lineage sister of one's foster son, and (3) the foster sister of one's lineage son. In all these, marriage is valid. However, if we are dealing with a lineage son's lineage sister (biological daughter or stepdaughter), then marriage is prohibited. The reason is that if the sister is from the same father's sperm, she is his own daughter. If she is from a different father but shares the same mother, she is a stepdaughter (rabibah), and if the father had intercourse with the mother, the stepdaughter becomes prohibited. This reasoning does not apply in fosterage because the fosterage bond does not create such direct paternity or marital relationships. Therefore, marriage to a foster son's sister is permissible.

Key Terms
ربیبہ (rabibah): Stepdaughter: the daughter of one's spouse from a previous marriage; she becomes prohibited if one had intercourse with her mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to marry the sister of one's foster son according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the foster son is not a real son
B) Because the reason for prohibition in lineage (intercourse with the mother) is absent in fosterage
C) Because the sister is not related by blood
D) Because the foster son's sister is never a close relative

Key Takeaway
Marriage to the sister of a foster son is permissible because the reason for prohibition from lineage (intercourse with her mother) does not exist in fosterage.

Marriage to Wife of Foster Father or Foster Son is Prohibited
Establishing prohibition of marriage to wife of foster father and wife of foster son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage to the wife of a foster father or foster son and explain the proof from hadith and the Quranic interpretation.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates marriage prohibitions identical to lineage, supplementing the Quran's biological focus.

The passage from al-Hidayah establishes that marriage to the wife of one's foster father or foster son is absolutely prohibited, just as in lineage. The Quranic verse (4:23) mentions 'wives of your sons from your loins,' which could be misinterpreted as limiting prohibition to biological sons. The Hanafi school resolves this by relying on the famous hadith that equates fosterage and lineage prohibitions, and explains that the Quranic restriction was to address the pre-Islamic custom of adoption, not fosterage. This lesson unpacks the interplay of Quran and Sunnah in deducing a clear ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited marriages
The passage lists two cases: marrying the wife of one's foster father, and marrying the wife of one's foster son. Note that 'foster father' refers to the husband of the woman who nursed you, and 'foster son' refers to a male child you nursed.
The prohibition mirrors that of biological relations.
2
Understand the general principle from hadith
The hadith 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage' establishes that fosterage creates the same marital restrictions as biological relation. This is the primary proof for the prohibition.
This hadith is ahad (single-chained) but its meaning is considered decisive (qat'i al-dalalah) in the Hanafi school.
3
Resolve the apparent Quranic restriction
The Quran (4:23) says 'the wives of your sons from your loins.' This seems to restrict prohibition to biological sons. The commentator explains that the phrase 'from your loins' was revealed to abrogate the pre-Islamic practice of considering adopted sons as real sons, not to limit fosterage prohibitions. Thus, the hadith supplements the Quran.
The Hanafi interpretation distinguishes between adopted sons (mutabanna) and foster sons (radi').
4
Recognise the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is: Hanafis prohibit marriage to the wife of a foster son via the hadith, while Shafi'is consider the Quranic restriction exhaustive and may not prohibit it unless by other evidence. This highlights the importance of understanding the sources.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi and widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رضاعی باپ کی بیوی اور رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی سے نکاح ناجائز ہے
و امرأة ابيه اوامرأة ابنه من الرضاع لا يجوزان يتزوجها كما لا يجوز ذلك من النسب الماروينا و ذكر الاصلاب فى النص لاسقاط اعتبار التبنى على مابيناه
ترجمہ اور اپنے رضاعی باپ کی بیوی یا رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ یہ نسب سے جائز نہیں ۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور آیت میں اصلاب کا ذکر متبنیٰ کے اعتبار کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے ہے اسی تفصیل پر جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح وامرأۃ ابیہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مرضعہ ( دودھ پلانے والی) کے شوہر نے دوسری شادی ہندہ کے ساتھ کی ہے۔ پھر ہندہ کو طلاق دے دی تو اس مرضعہ کا رضاعی بیٹا ہندہ کے ساتھ نکاح نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ ہندہ اس کے رضاعی باپ کی بیوی ہے۔ اسی طرح رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کے ساتھ نکاح حرام ہے۔ دلیل حدیث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب ہے۔ وذكر الا صلاب سے صاحب ہدایہ نے ایک سوال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ کلام پاک میں محرمات نساء کا ذکر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا و حلائل ابنائكم الذين من اصلابكم اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صرف صلبی بیٹے کی بیوی حرام ہے۔ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی حرام نہیں ہے ۔ حالانکہ حکم اس کے خلاف ہے۔ جواب آیت میں اصلاب کی قید متبنی کی بیوی کو خارج کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کو ۔ حاصل یہ کہ متبنی کی بیوی حلال ہے اور صلبی بیٹے کی بیوی کے ساتھ نکاح کی حرمت کتاب اللہ سے ثابت ہے اور رضاعی بیٹے کی بیوی کی حرمت مشہور حدیث يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب سے ثابت ہے۔
Marriage to the wife of one's foster father and the wife of one's foster son is not permissible. 'And the wife of his father or the wife of his son from fosterage, it is not permissible for him to marry them, just as it is not permissible from lineage, due to the hadith we narrated. And the mention of 'loins' (al-Aslab) in the text is to negate the consideration of adoption, as we have explained.' Translation: And marriage to the wife of one's foster father or the wife of one's foster son is not permissible, just as it is not permissible from lineage, because of the hadith we have narrated. And the mention of 'loins' in the verse is to cancel the consideration of adoption, according to the detail we have explained. Explanation: The case of the wife of the father: a foster child's foster mother's husband married another woman, Hind, then divorced her. So the foster son of the foster mother should not marry Hind, because Hind is the wife of his foster father. Similarly, marriage to the wife of a foster son is prohibited. The proof is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage.' And the mention of 'loins' (al-Aslab) is used by the author of al-Hidayah to answer a question: In the Quran, when listing prohibited women, it says 'and the wives of your sons who are from your loins.' This implies only the wife of a biological son is prohibited, not the wife of a foster son, yet the ruling is contrary. The answer is that the qualification 'from your loins' is to exclude the wife of an adopted son, not the wife of a foster son. The conclusion: the wife of an adopted son is permissible, the prohibition of the wife of a biological son is established by the Quran, and the prohibition of the wife of a foster son is established by the famous hadith 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage addresses two prohibitions: marriage to the wife of one's foster father and marriage to the wife of one's foster son. The base text from al-Hidayah states they are prohibited just as in lineage, citing the hadith 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage.' The commentary provides an example: a woman's foster son cannot marry the woman his foster father married and later divorced, as she is his foster father's wife. The key issue is that the Quranic verse (4:23) mentions 'the wives of your sons from your loins,' which seems to restrict prohibition to biological sons. The commentator explains that this qualification is to exclude adopted sons, not foster sons. Therefore, the prohibition for foster sons is derived from the hadith, not the Quran directly. This shows the interaction between Quran and Sunnah in establishing rulings. The adopted son's wife is halal, but the foster son's wife is haram.

Key Terms
صلب (sulb): Loins; refers to biological descent. In the Quranic verse, it specifies sons from one's own loins, excluding adopted sons.
متبنی (mutabanna): Adopted son; a child legally adopted in pre-Islamic custom. Islam abolished this practice concerning marriage prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used in the Hanafi school to prohibit marriage to the wife of a foster son?
A) The Quranic verse 4:23 interpreted literally
B) The hadith 'What is prohibited by fosterage is what is prohibited by lineage'
C) Consensus (ijma) of the companions
D) Analogy (qiyas) with adopted sons

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits marriage to the wife of a foster father or foster son, relying on the hadith equating fosterage prohibitions to lineage, and interpreting the Quranic 'from your loins' as excluding adopted sons only.

The Milk of the Sire and Its Effect on Prohibition
Explaining that the milk of the sire creates prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on laban al-fahl and identify its effect on prohibition, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The milk of the sire creates prohibition, making the wet nurse's husband a foster father.

This passage introduces a key Muslim legal concept: the milk of the sire (laban al-fahl) establishes fosterage relationships and prohibitions on marriage. The Hanafi school holds that the husband of the wet nurse becomes a foster father, and his relatives become foster relatives. This differs from one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i, leading to practical differences in marriage eligibility.

Guided Path
1
Define laban al-fahl
Understand that 'laban al-fahl' refers to the milk produced as a result of the wet nurse's pregnancy from her husband. The milk is attributed to the husband (the sire) in matters of prohibition.
The term 'fahl' means sire or male progenitor.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, when a woman nurses a child, the prohibition extends to her husband (the sire) and his relatives (fathers, sons, etc.), making them foster mahrams.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Identify the primary dalil
The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Aisha: 'Let Aflah enter upon you, for he is your uncle from fosterage.' This shows that the fosterage relation goes through the sire.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
In one of his opinions, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the milk of the sire does not create prohibition, arguing that milk is part of the woman, not the man. The Hanafi response uses the hadith and analogy to lineage.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences (thamarah).
5
Apply the ruling to a case
If a woman nurses a baby girl, that baby girl cannot later marry the woman's husband (the sire) or his sons/grandsons. Under the Shafi'i view, these marriages would be permissible.
This shows the importance of the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لبن الفحل سے حرمت متعلق ہوتی ہے ، لبن الفحل کا مطلب
ولبن الفحل يتعلق به التحريم وهوان ترضع المرأة صبية فتحرم هذه الصبية على زوجها وعلى آبائه وابنائه ويصير الزوج الذى نزل لها منه اللبن اباللمرضعة وفى احد قولى الشافعى لبن الفحل لا يحرم لان الحرمة بشهة البعضية واللبن بعضها لا بعضه ولنا ماروينا والحرمة بالنسب من الجانبين فكذا بالرضاع وقوله عليه السلام لعائشة رضي الله عنها ليلج عليك افلح فانه عمك من الرضاعة ولانه سبب النزول اللبن منها فيضاف اليه فى موضع الحرمة احتياطا
Prohibition is attached to the milk of the sire (foster father). And the milk of the sire: it is when a woman nurses a girl, then that girl becomes prohibited to the woman's husband and to his fathers and his sons, and the husband from whom the milk originated becomes a father to the wet nurse. And in one of the two opinions of al-Shafi'i, the milk of the sire does not create prohibition because prohibition is due to the suspicion of being a part (of the body), and the milk is a part of the woman, not of the man. Our proof: what we have narrated (the hadith). And prohibition in lineage is from both sides, similarly in fosterage. And his saying (peace be upon him) to Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Let Aflah enter upon you, for he is your uncle from fosterage.' And because the milk originates from her and is attributed to him in the context of prohibition out of precaution.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of 'laban al-fahl' (milk of the sire). The term 'al-fahl' refers to the male who fathers the child, i.e., the husband of the wet nurse. The ruling is that when a woman nurses a child, the prohibition extends to the husband of that woman and his relatives. Thus, the husband becomes a foster father, and his relatives become foster relatives. This is a key difference with Imam al-Shafi'i, who in one of his opinions holds that the milk of the sire does not create prohibition, because the milk is a part of the woman's body, not the man's. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Aisha regarding Aflah, saying 'he is your uncle from fosterage,' indicates that the fosterage relation is established through the milk, and the man's connection is recognized. Second, just as lineage prohibition goes through both parents, so does fosterage. The text also notes that the milk comes from the woman but is attributed to the man in matters of prohibition as a precaution. This concept is crucial for determining which relatives become mahram through fosterage.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): Milk of the sire: the fosterage connection established through the husband of the wet nurse; his relatives become foster relatives.
فحل (fahl): Sire; the male who fathers the child; here, the husband of the wet nurse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof used by Hanafis to establish that the milk of the sire creates prohibition?
A) The Quranic verse about fosterage
B) The hadith of Aflah being called an uncle from fosterage
C) Logical analogy that milk comes from both parents
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The milk of the sire (laban al-fahl) creates prohibition, making the wet nurse's husband and his relatives mahram, based on the hadith of Aflah and the analogy with lineage.

Prohibition of Marrying Foster Father's or Foster Son's Wife
Ruling with proof: The text asserts prohibition and clarifies the role of the hadith over the Quranic exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the spouse of a foster relative and identify the hadith-based proof that extends lineage prohibitions to fosterage.

Core Idea
A foster relationship creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage, based on the hadith: 'What is forbidden by fosterage is forbidden by lineage.'

A common question in marriage law is whether fosterage creates the same prohibitions as biological lineage. The Hanafi school affirms this, citing a clear hadith. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains why the Quranic phrase 'from your loins' does not limit the prohibition to biological sons but rather excludes adopted sons only.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the statement of prohibition: the woman is unlawful to marry.
The text says 'لا يجوز أن يتزوجها'.
2
Locate the proof
The author references a hadith. Identify which hadith and its implication.
The hadith is 'يحرّم من الرضاع ما يحرّم من النسب'.
3
Understand the Quranic exclusion
The Quranic verse mentions 'from your loins' to exclude adopted sons, not foster sons. Why?
Adopted sons are not treated as biological sons; foster sons are treated as biological sons.
4
Distinguish from Shafi'i view
Note the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i on the scope of fosterage prohibitions.
Some Shafi'is argue the Quran limits to biological sons, but Hanafis say the hadith overrides.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that any marriage to a foster relative's spouse is haram based on the hadith.
This includes father's wife and son's wife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و امرأة ابيه اوامرأة ابنه من الرضاع لا يجوزان يتزوجها كما لا يجوز ذلك من النسب الماروينا و ذكر الاصلاب فى النص لاسقاط اعتبار التبنى على مابيناه
And the wife of his father or the wife of his son from fosterage, it is not permissible for him to marry her, just as that is not permissible from lineage, due to what we have narrated, and the mention of 'loins' in the text is to nullify the consideration of adoption, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that it is prohibited to marry the wife of one's foster father or the wife of one's foster son, just as it is prohibited in lineage (nasab). The proof is the hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' which the author refers to. The Quranic verse (4:23) mentions 'wives of your sons from your loins' to exclude the wife of an adopted son, not to exclude foster sons. Thus, the prohibition for foster sons is established by the hadith, not the Quran. The author clarifies that the phrase 'من اصلابكم' is to negate adoption (tabanni), not to limit the prohibition to biological sons only.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage: the relationship created by breastfeeding that establishes certain legal prohibitions akin to lineage.
اصلاب (aslab): Loins; used in Quran to indicate biological descent.
متبنى (mutabanna): Adopted son; a child legally adopted but not biologically related.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'يحرّم من الرضاع ما يحرّم من النسب' is the primary proof that fosterage creates the same marriage prohibitions as biological lineage.

6 min
Laban al-Fahl Establishes Fosterage Prohibition
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on laban al-fahl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on laban al-fahl and explain the proof from the hadith of Aflah.

Core Idea
The milk of the wet nurse's husband establishes fosterage prohibition just as lineage does from both parents.

This lesson examines the Hanafi view that fosterage prohibitions extend to the husband of the wet nurse. While some scholars restrict prohibitions to the woman, Hanafis rely on the hadith of Aflah and the analogy to lineage. Understanding this dispute clarifies who becomes a foster relative.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that laban al-fahl (the milk attributed to the husband) establishes fosterage prohibition, making the girl prohibited to the husband and his relatives.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i in one of his two opinions holds that laban al-fahl does not prohibit. His rationale is that prohibition is based on being a part (ba'diyyah) of the body, and milk is a part of the woman, not the man.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof relies on the physical origin of milk; since it comes from the woman, it cannot be attributed to the man.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis cite the hadith where the Prophet told Aisha that Aflah is her uncle from fosterage, showing that the husband becomes a foster relative. They also invoke the general hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' and the principle that the husband is the cause of the milk, so it is attributed to him out of precaution.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the Shafi'i view, a man could marry a woman who was breastfed by his wife. Hanafis forbid such a marriage because the husband becomes a foster father.
This shows the importance of the dispute in real-life marriage prohibitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبن الفحل يتعلق به التحريم وهوان ترضع المرأة صبية فتحرم هذه الصبية على زوجها وعلى آبائه وابنائه ويصير الزوج الذى نزل لها منه اللبن اباللمرضعة وفى احد قولى الشافعى لبن الفحل لا يحرم لان الحرمة بشهة البعضية واللبن بعضها لا بعضه ولنا ماروينا والحرمة بالنسب من الجانبين فكذا بالرضاع وقوله عليه السلام لعائشة رضي الله عنها ليلج عليك افلح فانه عمك من الرضاعة ولانه سبب النزول اللبن منها فيضاف اليه فى موضع الحرمة احتياطا
And the milk of the male (laban al-fahl) is attached to it the prohibition, and it is that a woman breastfeeds a girl, so this girl becomes prohibited to her husband and to his fathers and his sons, and the husband from whom the milk came down becomes a father to the nursling. And in one of the two sayings of al-Shafi'i, the milk of the male does not prohibit, because the prohibition is due to the resemblance of being a part, and the milk is a part of her, not a part of him. And our proof is what we narrated, and the prohibition due to lineage is from both sides, so likewise with fosterage. And his saying, peace be upon him, to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'Let Aflah enter upon you, for he is your uncle from fosterage.' And because he is the cause of the milk coming down from her, so it is attributed to him in the place of prohibition out of precaution.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of 'laban al-fahl' (milk of the male) and its role in establishing fosterage prohibitions. The ruling is that when a woman breastfeeds a child, that child becomes a foster relative to the woman's husband and his close relatives. The husband becomes a foster father to the nursling. This is the Hanafi position. The passage then presents the dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i in one of his opinions holds that laban al-fahl does not create prohibition. His reasoning is that the prohibition is based on being a 'part' of the person (al-ba'diyyah), and since milk comes from the woman, not the man, the man is not included. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: 1) The hadith 'يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب' which analogizes fosterage to lineage, and in lineage, prohibition flows from both father and mother. 2) The specific incident where the Prophet told Aisha that Aflah is her uncle from fosterage because his wife had breastfed Aisha. This shows that the husband (Aflah) becomes a foster relative even though the milk came from his wife. Additionally, the husband is the cause of the milk (through impregnation), so out of precaution, the milk is attributed to him in matters of prohibition.

Key Terms
لبن الفحل (laban al-fahl): The milk of the male; here it refers to the husband of the wet nurse, attributing the milk to him because he is the cause of its existence.
بعضية (ba'diyyah): The quality of being a part or portion; used in the argument that the milk is part of the woman, not the man.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; a legal principle used to attribute the milk to the husband out of caution to maintain prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by Hanafis to prove that laban al-fahl establishes prohibition?
A) The Quranic verse about fosterage.
B) The hadith where the Prophet tells Aisha that Aflah is her uncle from fosterage.
C) Logical reasoning that milk cannot be attributed to the man.
D) Consensus of all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Laban al-fahl establishes fosterage prohibition, extending the circle of foster relatives to include the wet nurse's husband.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Permissibility of Marrying the Sister of One's Foster Brother
States a ruling with qiyas to lineage permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of a foster brother and explain the qiyas jaliy used to derive it.

Core Idea
A foster brother's blood sister is permissible to marry — fosterage does not extend to blood relatives.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: a man may marry the sister of his foster brother. This is based on a qiyas (analogy) to the permissibility of marrying the maternal half-sister of one's paternal half-brother. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of mahram relationships created by fosterage.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text begins with the hukm: it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother. Note the clear, unconditional language.
The ruling is mubah (permissible), not prohibited or disliked.
2
Identify the qiyas structure
The author cites an analogous case from lineage (nasab): a man may marry the maternal half-sister of his paternal half-brother. This is the asl (original case). The far' (new case) is marrying the blood sister of a foster brother.
The asl is explicitly provided in the text.
3
Extract the illa (cause)
The illa is that the woman is not a mahram. In the asl, the maternal half-sister of the paternal half-brother is a stranger. In the far', the blood sister of the foster brother is also a stranger because fosterage does not extend to her.
Fosterage only creates mahram with the wet nurse, her husband, and their direct children.
4
Apply the illa to the far'
Since the illa (non-mahram) exists in both cases, the ruling of permissibility transfers from asl to far' via qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
This is a qiyas jaliy because the illa is explicit and shared.
5
Consider the practical implication
The ruling permits marriage to the blood sister of any foster sibling. However, the foster sibling himself is a mahram, and his mother (the wet nurse) is also a mahram. This distinction is crucial.
The ruling does not permit marriage to the wet nurse or her husband.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رضاعی بھائی کی بہن سے نکاح جائز ہے
ويجوزان يتزوج الرجل باخت اخيه من الرضاع لانه يجوزان يتزوج باخت اخيه من النسب وذلك مثل الاخ من الاب اذا كانت له أخت من امه جاز لاخيه من ابيه ان يتزوجها
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے کہ مرد نکاح کرے اپنے رضاعی بھائی کی بہن کے ساتھ ۔ کیونکہ اپنے نسبی بھائی کی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ مثلاً باپ شریکہ بھائی جب کہ اس کی ماں شریک ، بہن ہو تو اس کے باپ شریک بھائی کیلئے جائز ہے کہ اس سے نکاح کرے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ خالد نے ماجد کی ماں کا پیا تو ماجد خالد کی نسبی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ لڑ کی ماجد کے رضاعی بھائی خالد کی نسبی بہن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نبی بھائی کی نسبی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ شاہد کے دو بیٹے ہیں اور ماں دونوں کی الگ الگ ہے تو یہ دونوں علاقی بھائی ہوئے (باپ شریک) شاہد نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو طلاق دے دی۔ اس مطلقہ نے عدت گزارنے کے بعد کسی دوسرے خاوند سے نکاح کر لیا اور اس سے ایک لڑکی پیدا ہوگئی تو یہ لڑ کی شاہد کے دونوں بیٹوں میں سے ایک کی ماں شریکی بہن ہے۔ اور دوسرے کے حق میں اجنبیہ ہے۔ پس یہ دوسرا بیٹا اس لڑکی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ لڑکی اپنے شوہر کے نسبی بھائی کی نسبی بہن ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ لڑکی اسکے حق میں اجنبیہ عورت تھی جس سے اس کی شادی ہوئی ہے۔ اسلئے یہ نکاح درست ہے۔
Marrying the sister of one's foster brother is permissible. And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his brother from fosterage, because it is permissible for him to marry the sister of his brother from lineage. For example, a paternal half-brother: if he has a maternal half-sister, it is permissible for his paternal half-brother to marry her. Translation: It is permissible for a man to marry his foster brother's sister, because it is permissible for him to marry his blood brother's sister. For example, if a paternal half-brother has a maternal half-sister, it is permissible for his paternal half-brother to marry her. Explanation of the scenario: Khalid nursed from Majid's mother, so Majid can marry Khalid's blood sister, even though this girl is the blood sister of Majid's foster brother Khalid. The proof is that it is permissible to marry the blood sister of one's paternal half-brother. The scenario: A man named Shahid has two sons from different mothers, so they are paternal half-brothers. Shahid divorces one of their mothers. After her iddah, she marries another man and has a daughter. This daughter is the maternal half-sister of one of Shahid's sons, and a stranger to the other. So the other son can marry this daughter, even though she is the blood sister of his paternal half-brother. But because she is a stranger to him, the marriage is valid.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a man may marry the sister of his foster brother. The proof is based on analogy (qiyas) to a relative scenario. In lineage, a man may marry the sister of his paternal half-brother, because that sister is not a mahram to him. Similarly, a foster brother is only a mahram due to fosterage, but his blood sister is not a mahram to his foster brother. The passage provides a detailed example: A man named Khalid is nursed by Majid's mother. Therefore, Khalid becomes Majid's foster brother. Majid may marry Khalid's blood sister, because Khalid's blood sister is a stranger to Majid. The analogy is made to paternal half-brothers, where one brother's maternal half-sister is permissible for the other brother. The passage also gives a more complex scenario involving a divorce and remarriage to illustrate the permissibility. The ruling is straightforward: foster kinship does not extend to the blood relatives of a foster sibling.

Key Terms
رضاعی بھائی (rada'i bhai): Foster brother; a male who was nursed by the same woman as oneself.
نسبی بھائی (nasabi bhai): Blood brother; a male with a common parent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a man marry the blood sister of his foster brother?
A) No, because she is a mahram through fosterage.
B) Yes, because fosterage does not make the blood sister of a foster brother a mahram.
C) No, because she is considered a sister.
D) Yes, only if she is also a foster sister.

Key Takeaway
A foster brother's blood sister is not a mahram; therefore, marrying her is permissible.

Proof that the Wet Nurse's Husband is the Foster Father
Explaining hadith and rational proof for foster father status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith and rational evidence proving that the wet nurse's husband becomes the foster father, and explain the implication for marital prohibitions.

Core Idea
The husband of the wet nurse is the foster father — proven because the Prophet called his brother a foster uncle.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah establishes a critical rule of fosterage (rada'): the husband of the wet nurse acquires the status of foster father to the child she suckles. The author presents both a hadith from Aisha (RA) and a rational argument to cement this ruling. Understanding this proof structure is essential for correctly identifying mahram relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling being proven
The ultimate ruling is that the husband of the wet nurse becomes the foster father of the child, making marriage between them prohibited (tahrim).
This rule is essential for determining whom one may marry.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (saw) called Afleh Aisha's foster uncle. A foster uncle can only exist if the wet nurse's husband (Afleh's brother) is Aisha's foster father. This is an a fortiori (اولیٰ) argument: if prohibition attaches to the foster uncle, it attaches even more to the foster father.
The hadith is from Muslim and Nasa'i, transmitted by Aisha.
3
Analyze the rational proof
The husband is the cause of milk descending (because pregnancy occurs through him). Therefore, out of precaution, the milk is attributed to him in matters of prohibition.
This rational argument (dalil aqli) reinforces the textual proof.
4
Resolve the identity of Afleh
The passage clarifies that Afleh was the brother of Abu Qais (Abu Isa), not his son, as per the majority of narrations and the verification of Allama Ayni and Qurtubi. This correct lineage is crucial for the foster relationship to be correctly traced.
If Afleh were the son, the relationship would change; but the correct view is brother.
5
Apply the ruling
The wet nurse's husband is a mahram to the child, meaning he may see the child without hijab after puberty, and marriage between them is prohibited forever.
The same prohibition applies to the wet nurse's children from the same husband (foster siblings).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا کہ مجھ کوعورت نے دودھ پلایا ہے اور مرد نے دودھ نہیں پلایا ہے۔ پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم میرے پاس تشریف لائے تو میں نے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے سارا حال بیان کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ وہ تیرے چچا ہیں۔ افلح تیرے پاس بغیر پردہ کے آیا کرے گا۔ اس حدیث میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے افلح کو حضرت عائشہ کا رضاعی چچا کہا ہے۔ اور رضاعی چچا اس کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا ہے کہ مرضعہ (دودھ پلانے والی) کا شوہر حضرت عائشہ کا رضاعی باپ ہو۔ پس جب رضاعی چچا کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق ہے تو رضاعی باپ کے ساتھ بدرجہ اولی تحریم متعلق ہوگی۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ شوہر عورت سے دودھ اترنے کا سبب ہے۔ لہذا احتیاطاً موضع حرمت میں دودھ کو شوہر کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا۔ فوائد حدیث عائد میں افلح بفتح الهمزه و سكون الفاء والحاء ہے۔ افلح ابو عیس کے بیٹے ہیں جیسا کہ مسلم کی روایت ہے اور اکثر روایات میں ایسا ہی ہے اور نسائی میں مالک کے طریق سے ان افلح اخا ابی القعیس ہے۔ یعنی افلح ابو عیسی کے بھائی ہیں نہ کہ بیٹے۔ علامہ عینی شارح ہدایہ نے اس کو درست لکھا ہے۔ اور علامہ قرطبی نے بھی کہا کہ یہی صحیح ہے۔ صاحب فتح القدیر اور صاحب کفایہ نے جو حدیث ذکر فرمائی ہے اس میں بھی افلح کو ابو عیس کا بھائی ہونا ذکر کیا ہے۔ ليلج امر غائب ولوج (بمعنی دخول) سے ہے۔ اصل میں تھا لیلج وادیا اور کسرہ کے درمیان واقع ہونے کی وجہ سے گر گیا۔ افلح رفع کے ساتھ لیلج کا فاعل ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Aisha said that a woman suckled me and the man did not suckle me. Then the Prophet (saw) came to me and I told him the whole story, so he said: 'He is your uncle. Afleh may come to you without a veil.' In this hadith, the Prophet (saw) called Afleh Aisha's foster uncle. And a foster uncle cannot be unless the husband of the wet nurse is Aisha's foster father. So when prohibition is attached to the foster uncle, then with the foster father it is attached a fortiori. Rational proof: The husband is the cause of milk descending. Therefore, out of precaution, in the context of prohibition, milk is attributed to the husband. Benefits: In the hadith 'Aidh', Afleh with fatha on hamza, sukun on fa and ha. Afleh is the son of Abu Isa as in Muslim's narration and most narrations. In Nasa'i, through Malik, he is Afleh, brother of Abu Qais. That is, Afleh is the brother of Abu Isa, not son. Allama Ayni, commentator of Hidayah, wrote this as correct. And Allama Qurtubi also said this is correct. The authors of Fath al-Qadir and Kifayah also mentioned Afleh as brother of Abu Isa. 'Laylaj' is an imperative of 'waluj' (meaning entry). Originally it was 'liyulij' and the kasra dropped. Afleh is the subject of 'laylaj' in the nominative. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing that the husband of the wet nurse becomes the foster father of the child she suckles. The primary proof is a hadith in which the Prophet (saw) referred to Afleh as Aisha's foster uncle, which necessarily implies that Afleh's brother (the wet nurse's husband) is Aisha's foster father. The commentator then provides a rational proof (dalil aqli): the husband is the cause of the milk descending, so the milk is attributed to him in matters of prohibition. The passage also clarifies the identity of Afleh, resolving a difference in narrations as to whether he was the son or brother of Abu Qais (or Abu Isa). The relied-upon view (as per Allama Ayni and Qurtubi) is that Afleh was the brother, not the son. This is crucial because it affects the lineage of the foster relationship. The passage ends with a grammatical note on the word 'laylaj'.

Key Terms
مرضعہ (murdi'ah): The woman who suckles a child; the wet nurse.
رضاعی (rada'i): Related through fosterage (suckling), causing the same prohibitions as blood relations in specified cases.
تحریم (tahrim): Prohibition; here, the prohibition of marriage due to foster relationship.
اولی (awla): A fortiori; a logical argument that if something applies to a lesser case, it applies even more to a greater case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet (saw) call Afleh in relation to Aisha?
A) Foster father
B) Foster brother
C) Foster uncle
D) Foster son

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse's husband becomes the child's foster father, proven by the hadith of Aisha and a fortiori reasoning, making marriage between them permanently prohibited.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Marrying the Sister of a Foster Brother is Permissible
Stating and proving the permissibility of marrying the sister of a foster brother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of a foster brother and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
A foster brother's sister is a stranger to you; marriage is permissible.

This lesson clarifies a common point of confusion: the extent of mahram relationships through fosterage. While a foster mother and her direct foster children become mahrams, the siblings of a foster brother remain strangers. The Hanafi school proves this by analogy (qiyas) to the blood brother case, where a brother's sister (unless also your sister) is permissible for marriage. We will walk through this analogy step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
State the exact hukm (ruling) for the act of marrying the sister of one's foster brother. The text says 'yajuz' (it is permissible).
The ruling is permissibility (ibahah), not obligation or recommendation.
2
Locate the asl (original case) for the analogy
The author presents a blood brother scenario: a man is allowed to marry the half-sister of his half-brother (from the father side). Identify the parties and why she is not his mahram.
The asl is the permissibility of marrying the blood sister of a blood half-brother.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
What is the common reason that permits marriage in both cases? The text implies: the brother (whether blood or foster) does not make his sister a mahram to his brother. The sister remains a stranger (ajnabiyyah) to his brother.
The illa is that the bond between brothers does not extend to their respective sisters as mahram.
4
Apply the illa to the far' (new case)
The far' is marrying the blood sister of a foster brother. Since the illa is the same (brotherhood does not create mahram status between the brother's sister), the ruling of permissibility transfers.
This is a clear qiyas jaliyy (obvious analogy).
5
Confirm the ruling and note the proof
Conclude that marrying the sister of a foster brother is permissible. The proof is the qiyas given, supported by the general principle that marriage with non-mahrams is permitted until proven forbidden.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوزان يتزوج الرجل باخت اخيه من الرضاع لانه يجوزان يتزوج باخت اخيه من النسب وذلك مثل الاخ من الاب اذا كانت له أخت من امه جاز لاخيه من ابيه ان يتزوجها ترجمہ اور جائز ہے کہ مرد نکاح کرے اپنے رضاعی بھائی کی بہن کے ساتھ۔ کیونکہ اپنے نسبی بھائی کی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہ مثلاً باپ شریکہ بھائی جب کہ اس کی ماں شریک، بہن ہو تو اس کے باپ شریک بھائی کیلئے جائز ہے کہ اس سے نکاح کرے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ خالد نے ماجد کی ماں کا دودھ پیا تو ماجد خالد کی نسبی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ لڑکی ماجد کے رضاعی بھائی خالد کی نسبی بہن ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نسبی بھائی کی نسبی بہن کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ شاہد کے دو بیٹے ہیں اور ماں دونوں کی الگ الگ ہے تو یہ دونوں علاقی بھائی ہوئے (باپ شریک) شاہد نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو طلاق دے دی۔ اس مطلقہ نے عدت گزارنے کے بعد کسی دوسرے خاوند سے نکاح کر لیا اور اس سے ایک لڑکی پیدا ہوگئی تو یہ لڑکی شاہد کے دونوں بیٹوں میں سے ایک کی ماں شریکی بہن ہے۔ اور دوسرے کے حق میں اجنبیہ ہے۔ پس یہ دوسرا بیٹا اس لڑکی سے نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ لڑکی اپنے شوہر کے نسبی بھائی کی نسبی بہن ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ لڑکی اسکے حق میں اجنبیہ عورت تھی جس سے اس کی شادی ہوئی ہے۔ اسلئے یہ نکاح درست ہے۔
And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother, because it is permissible for him to marry the sister of his blood brother. For example, a half-brother from the father, if he has a half-sister from the mother, it is permissible for his half-brother from the father to marry her. Translation: And it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother, because it is permissible to marry the sister of his blood brother. For example, a half-brother from the father, if he has a half-sister from the mother, it is permissible for his half-brother from the father to marry her. Explanation: The scenario of the issue is that Khalid suckled from Maja's mother, so Majid can marry Khalid's blood sister, even though this girl is the sister of Majid's foster brother Khalid. The proof is that it is permissible to marry the blood sister of a blood brother. The scenario is that Shahid has two sons from different mothers, so they are half-brothers (from father). Shahid divorced one of them. This divorced woman, after completing her iddah, married another husband and had a daughter. This daughter is the half-sister from the mother of one of Shahid's sons, and a stranger to the other. So the other son can marry this daughter, even though she is the blood sister of his blood brother. This marriage is valid.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof by analogy (qiyas). It states the ruling: it is permissible for a man to marry the sister of his foster brother. The proof is that the same is allowed with a blood brother: if a man has a half-brother from the father, and that half-brother has a half-sister from the mother (who is not the man's sister), the man can marry her. Similarly, if a man (Majid) had a foster brother (Khalid) who suckled from Majid's mother, then Khalid's blood sister is not a mahram to Majid, so he may marry her. The commentary provides a detailed example to clarify the application of the analogy, emphasizing that the prohibition of marriage due to fosterage does not extend beyond the specific relationships defined by the texts.

Key Terms
رضاعی بھائی (rada'i bhai): Foster brother; a male who shared the same wet nurse.
نسبی (nasabi): Related by blood lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to marry the sister of one's foster brother?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, it is prohibited
C) It is disliked
D) It depends on the wet nurse's consent

Key Takeaway
Marrying the sister of a foster brother is permissible because the foster relationship does not make her a mahram, analogous to the blood brother case.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Two Children Suckling from Same Woman Cannot Marry
Stating the prohibition of foster-sibling marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding marriage between foster siblings who shared the same wet nurse, and explain the principle (asl) behind it.

Core Idea
Foster siblings, like blood siblings, cannot marry—the milk relationship creates a permanent prohibition.

This passage establishes a fundamental rule in the chapter of fosterage (rida'): any boy and girl who have both suckled from the same woman become mahram (unmarriageable kin). The rule is straightforward but carries deep implications for family relations in Islam. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the laws of marriage and prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is two children (boy and girl) who have both suckled from one woman. The ruling: it is not permissible (la yajuza) for one to marry the other.
2
Understand the principle (asl)
The text states 'hadha huwa al-asl' (this is the principle). The principle is that sharing the same milk mother makes them foster siblings, analogous to blood siblings.
3
Recognize the basis (illa)
The reason: 'because their mother is one, so they are brother and sister.' The mother is the same, thus they are siblings.
4
Note the scope
This applies regardless of whether they suckled simultaneously or at different times, as long as both suckled from the same woman, as clarified in the commentary.

Source Text

و كل صبيين اجتمعا على ثدى امرأة واحدة لم يجز لاحدهما ان يتزوج بالأخرى هذا هو الاصل لان امهما واحدة فهما اخ واخت ترجمہ اور ہر وہ دو بچے (لڑکا اور لڑکی) جو ایک عورت کے پستان پر جمع ہو گئے تو ان دونوں میں ایک کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ دوسرے کیساتھ نکاح کرے۔ اور یہی (باب حرمت) میں اصل ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں کی ماں ایک ہے۔ پس وہ دونوں بھائی، بہن ہوئے۔ تشریح دونوں بچوں یعنی لڑکا اور لڑکی نے کسی عورت کا دودھ پیا ایک ساتھ یا آگے پیچھے تو یہ دونوں رضاعی بھائی بہن ہوں گے اور ان کا نکاح آپس میں درست نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ نسبی بھائی بہن آپس میں نکاح نہیں کر سکتے ہیں۔ باب حرمت میں یہی ضابطہ ہے۔
And every two children (boy and girl) who assemble on the breast of one woman, it is not permissible for one of them to marry the other. This is the principle (in the chapter of prohibitions) because their mother is one, so they are brother and sister. Translation: And every two children (boy and girl) who gather on the breast of one woman, it is not permissible for one of them to marry the other. This is the principle (in the chapter of prohibition) because their mother is one, so they are brother and sister. Explanation: Two children, i.e., a boy and a girl, who drank milk from a woman, either together or one after the other, will be foster brother and sister, and their marriage with each other will not be valid. Just as blood brother and sister cannot marry each other. This is the rule in the chapter of prohibitions.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling statement that forms a foundational rule in the chapter of fosterage. It states that any boy and girl who have both suckled from the same woman become foster siblings, and marriage between them is prohibited. The principle is based on the analogy to blood siblings: just as a brother and sister by blood cannot marry, neither can foster siblings. The commentary clarifies that it does not matter whether they suckled simultaneously or at different times; the prohibition is established.

Key Terms
صبیین (sabiyyayn): Two children; in this context, one male and one female who have been suckled.
اصل (asl): The fundamental principle or rule in the chapter of prohibitions regarding fosterage.

Foster Marriage Prohibitions: Extended Family
Stating prohibitions for foster child regarding wet nurse's family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which relatives of the wet nurse are prohibited in marriage for the foster child, and explain the reasoning by analogy to blood relations.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates sibling and avuncular prohibitions like blood: wet nurse's children = siblings, grandchildren = nieces/nephews, husband's sister = paternal aunt.

This passage from al-Hidayah lists several marriage prohibitions arising from fosterage. While a wet nurse herself is a foster mother, the restrictions extend beyond her immediate relationship. The ruling uses qiyas (analogy) to blood family ties: just as marriage is prohibited to blood siblings and aunts, so too are these foster relationships. Understanding these prohibitions is essential to avoid invalid marriages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foster child (al-murdi'ah)
Determine the grammatical subject/object ambiguity, but note the prohibition is mutual.
The text's commentary clarifies both readings yield the same prohibition.
2
List prohibited relatives
Enumerate: children of wet nurse, grandchildren, and sister of wet nurse's husband.
For a female foster child, the first two apply; for a male, the third applies.
3
State the basis for each prohibition
Explain the analogy: wet nurse's child = brother, grandchild = nephew, husband's sister = paternal aunt.
These are analogies to blood relationships.
4
Confirm the mutual nature
The prohibition is bidirectional: foster child cannot marry wet nurse's relatives, and vice versa.
The grammatical analysis supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لا يتزوج المرضعة احدا من ولدالتي رضعت لانه اخوها ولا ولدولدها لانه ولداخيها ولا يتزوج الصبى المرضع اخت زوج المرضعة لانها عمته من الرضاع ترجمہ اور نہ نکاح کرے مرضعہ (جس کو دودھ پلایا گیا) کسی سے اس عورت کے لڑکوں میں سے جس نے (اس کو) دودھ پلایا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ لڑکا اس کا بھائی ہے۔ اور نہ اس دودھ پلانے والی کی اولاد سے کیونکہ یہ اس کا بھتیجا ہے۔ اور نہ نکاح کرے وہ بچہ جس کو دودھ پلایا گیا ہے۔ دودھ پلانے والی کے شوہر کی بہن سے کیونکہ وہ اس کی رضاعی پھوپھی ہے۔ تشریح المرضعہ میں ترکیب کے اعتبار سے دو احتمال ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ مرضعہ الفتح النضاد اسم مفعول ہے۔ و بتروج کا فاعل ہونے کی وجہ سے مرفوع ہو اور احد منصوب ہو مفعولیت کی بناء پر اس صورت میں ترجمہ ہو گا کہ صبیہ مرضعہ دودھ پلانے والی کے لڑکوں میں سے کسی کے ساتھ نکاح نہ کرے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ مرضعہ بصیغہ اسم مفعول منصوب ہو مفعولیت کی بنا پر اور احد مرفوع ہو فاعلیت کی بناء پر۔ اس صورت میں ترجمہ ہو گا کہ دودھ پلانے والی عورت کے لڑکوں میں سے کوئی صبیہ مرضعہ کے ساتھ نکاح نہ کرے۔ حاصل دونوں کا ایک ہے۔ مسئلہ کی صورت اور اس کی دلیل دونوں واضح ہیں۔ محتاج بیان نہیں ہے۔
And the foster child (female) should not marry any of the sons of the woman who suckled her, because he is her brother. Nor should she marry the child of that woman's child, because he is her nephew. And the foster child (male) should not marry the sister of the wet nurse's husband, because she is his foster paternal aunt. Translation: And the foster child should not marry any of the sons of the woman who suckled her, because that son is her brother. Nor should she marry the child of that woman's child, because that is her nephew. And the foster male child should not marry the sister of the wet nurse's husband, because she is his foster paternal aunt. Explanation: In the phrase 'almurdi'ah (المرضعہ)', there are two possibilities regarding grammatical construction. First, 'maradi'ah' is the object of 'tatazawwaj' and is in the nominative as subject, and 'ahad' is accusative as object. In this case, the translation is: The female foster child should not marry any of the sons of the woman who suckled her. Second, 'maradi'ah' is accusative as object, and 'ahad' is nominative as subject. Then the translation is: Any son of the wet nurse should not marry the female foster child. The result of both is the same. The scenario and its proof are clear and need no explanation.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating several prohibitions resulting from fosterage. It states that the foster child (whether male or female) cannot marry the direct children of the wet nurse (i.e., her sons and daughters), nor can she marry the wet nurse's grandchildren (as they are nephews/nieces). Additionally, the male foster child cannot marry the sister of the wet nurse's husband (his foster paternal aunt). The commentary discusses a grammatical ambiguity in the Arabic phrase 'مرضعہ' (al-murdi'ah) as to whether it should be read as the subject or object, but concludes that in both readings, the prohibition remains mutual: the foster child cannot marry the wet nurse's children and vice versa. The proof for these prohibitions is analogy to blood relationships: the wet nurse's children are the foster child's siblings, and the wet nurse's husband's sister is like a paternal aunt.

Key Terms
مرضعہ (murdi'ah): In this passage, it refers to the female foster child (the one who was suckled).
ولد (walad): Child; here, specifically the wet nurse's direct children and also her grandchildren (ولد الولد).
عمتہ من الرضاع (ammatuhu min al-rada'): His foster paternal aunt; the sister of the wet nurse's husband.
