Milk Mixed with Water: Majority Determines Prohibition
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on fosterage when milk is mixed with water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fosterage when milk is mixed with water and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school, applying the principle that the majority determines legal existence.

Core Idea
In a mixture, the majority governs: if water dominates, milk is legally nonexistent and no fosterage arises.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on a mixture of milk and water. The question: does a child drinking such a mixture establish a foster relationship? The answer hinges on whether the milk is the majority component. The Hanafi school applies the principle that the minority is legally nonexistent when overwhelmed, analogous to oaths. This passage from the Hidayah presents the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a child drinks a mixture of milk and water. Ruling: if milk is majority, fosterage prohibition (tahrim) applies; if water majority, no prohibition.
2
Locate the opposing school
Al-Shafi'i holds that any presence of milk triggers prohibition, regardless of proportion.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The minority (maghlub) is legally non-existent (ma'dum hukman) when overwhelmed by the majority (ghalib), as in oaths.
The analogy to oaths reinforces the principle.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Milk exists in reality (haqiqatan) in the mixture, so its effect is present.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if water is majority, Hanafi says no fosterage; Shafi'i says fosterage established.
This changes which marriages are prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اختلط اللبن بالماء واللبن هو الغالب تعلق به التحريم وان غلب الماء لم يتعلق به التحريم خلافا للشافعي هو يقول انه موجود فيه حقيقة ونحن نقول المغلوب غير موجود حكما حتى لا يظهر بمقابلة الغالب كمافى اليمين ترجمہ اور اگر دودھ پانی کے ساتھ مخلوط ہو گیا اور حال یہ کہ دودھ غالب ہے تو اس کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق ہوگی اور اگر پانی غالب ہے تو تحریم اس کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوگی خلاف ہے شافعی کا وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دودھ اس میں حقیقتا موجود ہے اور ہم کہیں گے کہ مغلوب حکما غیر
And if milk is mixed with water, and the milk is the majority, then prohibition is attached to it. And if water is the majority, prohibition is not attached to it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He says that it (milk) exists in it in reality. And we say that the overwhelmed (minority) is non-existent in legal consideration, so it does not appear in confrontation with the majority, as in oaths. Translation: And if milk is mixed with water, and the milk is the majority, then the prohibition (of fosterage) is attached to it. And if water is the majority, then the prohibition is not attached to it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He says that milk exists in it in reality. And we say that the minor component is legally considered non-existent, so it does not appear in opposition to the majority, as in oaths.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a mixture of milk and water that is drunk by a child. The ruling is that if the mixture is predominantly milk, then the prohibition of fosterage (tahrim) applies as if it were pure milk. If water is the majority, then prohibition does not apply. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that as long as milk is present in the mixture, even if it is a minority, prohibition applies because milk exists in reality. The Hanafi response is that the minority component (milk) is legally considered non-existent (ma'dum hukman) when overwhelmed by the majority, similar to the ruling on oaths (yamin) where the majority determines the legal effect. The passage is incomplete, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms
غالب (ghalib): The majority component in a mixture; determines the ruling.
مغلوب (maghlub): The minority component; legally non-existent when overwhelmed.
حکماً (hukman): Legally, in terms of legal consideration, as opposed to literal existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Mixing Milk with Food and Fosterage Prohibition
Explaining ruling when milk mixed with food, with proofs from Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fosterage prohibition when milk is mixed with food and explain the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The intended purpose (nutrition) determines the ruling: food is principal, milk subordinate; thus no fosterage prohibition.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: when human milk is mixed with food, does fosterage prohibition arise? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position based on the intended purpose of the mixture. You will learn the ruling for both cooked and uncooked food, the proofs of the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa, and the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Scenario
Understand the two scenarios: milk mixed with uncooked food, and milk mixed with cooked food. Also consider the sub-issue of dripping milk from a morsel.
2
State the Hanafi Position
According to Abu Hanifa, fosterage prohibition is not established whether milk is dominant or overwhelmed in uncooked food. For cooked food, consensus that prohibition does not attach.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's Proof
The Sahibayn argue that consideration is given to the dominant component, analogous to water mixed with milk. They hold that if milk is dominant in uncooked food, prohibition attaches.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's Proof and Response
Abu Hanifa argues that the intended purpose (nutrition) is from food, making milk subordinate even if quantitatively dominant. Thus prohibition does not attach.
5
Note Intra-Hanafi Difference and Mufta Bihi
Abu Hanifa has another view that a single drop of milk entering the throat establishes prohibition, but the relied-upon view is non-prohibition in all cases, including dripping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ اس کو آگ نے مس ( چھونا ) نہ کیا ہو۔ حتی کہ اگر ( مخلوط دودھ طعام ) کو آگ سے پکالیا گیا ہو تو بالا تفاق اس کے تحریم متعلق نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتبار غالب کا ہے۔ جیسا کہ پانی میں جبکہ اس دودھ کو کسی چیز نے اپنے حال سے متغیر نہ کیا ہو۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طعام اصل ہے۔ اور دودھ حق مقصود ( تغذی) میں اسکے تابع ہے۔ پس ( دودھ ) مغلوب ہو گیا اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک طعام سے دودھ کے قطرے ٹپکنے کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ تغذی طعام سے ہوتی ہے اسلئے کہ طعام ہی اصل ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر دودھ کھانے میں مخلوط ہو گیا اور اس مخلوط دودھ کو آگ نے مس نہیں کیا۔ یعنی آگ پر پکایا نہیں گیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس سے حرمت رضاعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ دودھ کھانے میں غالب رہا ہو یا مغلوب۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں که اگر دودھ غالب ہے تو اسکے ساتھ تحریم متعلق ہو جائے گی ورنہ نہیں۔ اور اگر دودھ کھانے میں ملا کر آگ پر پکا لیا گیا تو بالاتفاق اس سے حرمت رضاعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔ دودھ غالب رہا ہو یا مغلوب۔ اسلئے کہ اگر دودھ مغلوب ہے تب تو حرمت کا ثابت نہ ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ اور اگر دودھ غالب ہے تو اسلئے حرمت ثابت نہیں ہوگی کہ جب دودھ کھانے میں ملا کر پکا لیا گیا تو دودھ کھانے کے تابع ہو گیا۔ لہذا اب این دودھ کو لبن مطلق نہیں کہہ سکتے ہیں ۔ اصل مسئلہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتبار غالب کا ہے جیسا کہ پانی میں غالب کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔ بشرطیکہ دودھ کوکسی چیز فنے اپنی حالت سے متغیر نہ کیا ہو۔ امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود یعنی غذا حاصل کرنے میں کھانا اصل ہے اور دودھ اس کے تابع ہے۔ لہذا حصول مقصود یعنی غذا میں دودھ مغلوب ہو گیا اگر چہ حقیقت میں غالب تھا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق نہیں ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر دودھ کھانے میں ملا ہوا ہے اور لقمہ اٹھاتے وقت کھانے سے دودھ کے قطرے ٹپکتے ہیں تو اس صورت میں حرمت رضاعت ثابت ہوگی یا نہیں؟ تو فرمایا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ حرمت رضاعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور تقاطر لین کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی غذا کھانے سے حاصل کی گئی ہے نہ کہ دودھ سے۔ کیونکہ غذا حاصل کرنے میں کھانا ہی اصل ہے۔ امام صاحب کا غیر اصح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ دودھ کا ایک قطرہ جب بچہ کے حلق میں داخل ہو گیا تو اثبات حرمت کیلئے کافی ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ ہر حال میں عدم ثبوت حرمت ہے۔
فوائد... فصار كالمغلوب میں کاف زائدہ ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
This case is when it has not been touched by fire. Even if the mixed mixture was cooked with fire, then by consensus prohibition will not attach. The evidence of the two companions is that consideration is given to the dominant. As in water, when the milk has not been changed from its state by something. And the evidence of Abu Hanifa is that food is the principal, and milk in terms of the intended purpose (nutrition) is subordinate to it. Therefore the milk becomes overwhelmed. And according to Imam Sahib [Abu Hanifa], dripping drops of milk from food is not considered; this is correct. Because nutrition comes from food, since food is the principal.
Explanation: The scenario of the issue is that if milk is mixed into food and that mixed milk has not been touched by fire, i.e., not cooked, then according to Imam Sahib, fosterage prohibition will not be established from it, whether the milk is dominant in the food or overwhelmed. And the two companions say that if the milk is dominant, then prohibition will attach to it; otherwise not. And if the milk is mixed into food and cooked on fire, then by consensus fosterage prohibition will not be established, whether the milk is dominant or overwhelmed. Because if the milk is overwhelmed, then it is obvious that prohibition is not established. And if the milk is dominant, then prohibition is not established because when milk is mixed into food and cooked, the milk becomes subordinate to the food. Therefore now this milk cannot be called absolute milk. In the original issue, the evidence of the two companions is that consideration is given to the dominant, as in water consideration is given to the dominant, provided that the milk has not been changed from its state by something. The evidence of Imam Sahib is that in obtaining the intended purpose (nutrition), food is the principal and milk is subordinate to it. Therefore, in achieving the intended purpose (nutrition), milk is overwhelmed even if it was actually dominant. For this reason, prohibition will not attach to it.
Sahib al-Hidayah asks: If milk is mixed into food and when lifting the morsel, drops of milk drip from the food, then in this case will fosterage prohibition be established or not? He said that according to Imam Sahib, the correct view is that fosterage prohibition is not established, and dripping of milk is not considered. The evidence is that in this case too, nutrition is obtained from food, not from milk. Because in obtaining nutrition, food is the principal. Another view of Imam Sahib, which is not the correct one, is that in this case prohibition is established. Because if one drop of milk enters the child's throat, that is sufficient for establishing prohibition. But the correct view is that in all cases, there is no establishment of prohibition.
Benefits: In 'fasara ka al-maghlub', the kaf is extra. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of fosterage prohibition (حرمت رضاعت) when human milk is mixed with food. The discussion has two parts: mixing with uncooked food and mixing with cooked food. 

First, for uncooked food: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that fosterage prohibition does not arise, regardless of whether the milk is dominant or overwhelmed. His reasoning is that the intended purpose (nutrition) is primarily from food; milk is subordinate even if it appears dominant. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: they say that if the milk is dominant in the mixture, prohibition attaches; if the milk is overwhelmed, it does not. Their proof is the principle of considering the dominant, analogous to water mixed with milk. The text notes that this is the same principle used in rulings about water.

Second, for cooked food: there is consensus that prohibition does not attach, whether milk is dominant or overwhelmed. Once cooked, milk loses its independent status and becomes fully subordinate to the food, so it can no longer be considered absolute milk for fosterage purposes.

The passage then addresses a sub-issue: if the milk-food mixture is such that when a morsel is lifted, milk drips from it. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, even these dripping drops do not establish prohibition, because the nutrition is still from the food, not from the milk separately. He is reported to have another view that even one drop entering the throat suffices for prohibition, but the correct relied-upon view is the former.

Finally, a grammatical note: in the phrase 'fasara ka al-maghlub', the 'kaf' is extra ( زائدہ ).

Key Terms
لبن (laban): Human milk; the milk that, when ingested by a child, creates fosterage relationships
طعام (ta'am): Food; the substance into which milk is mixed in this scenario
غالب (ghalib): Dominant; the component in a mixture that is greater in quantity or effect
مغلوب (maghlub): Overwhelmed; the component in a mixture that is subordinate in quantity or effect
تحریم رضاعت (tahrim al-rada'ah): Fosterage prohibition; the legal impediment to marriage that arises from breastfeeding
تقاطر (taqatur): Dripping; the falling of milk droplets from a morsel

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when human milk is mixed with uncooked food, what is the ruling on fosterage prohibition?
A) Prohibition is established if the milk is dominant in the mixture
B) Prohibition is not established regardless of whether the milk is dominant or overwhelmed
C) Prohibition is established only if the milk is overwhelmed
D) Prohibition is established if any drop of milk reaches the child's throat

Key Takeaway
Human milk mixed with food does not establish fosterage prohibition in the Hanafi school because food remains the principal source of nutrition, making milk subordinate.

Milk Mixed with Medicine: Fosterage Prohibition Conditional on Purpose
Clarifying that when milk mixed with medicine, prohibition depends on which is dominant and the intended purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that fosterage prohibition depends on the dominant component and intended purpose when milk is mixed with medicine.

Core Idea
Fosterage prohibition turns on whether milk is the intended source of nutrition, not mere presence.

This lesson examines a nuanced case: human milk mixed with medicine. Does a drop of milk always create a fosterage prohibition? The Hanafi school says no—the ruling hinges on which ingredient is dominant and why the mixture is given. Understanding this principle sharpens your grasp of intention and dominance in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is feeding an infant a mixture of human milk and medicine. The ruling is that fosterage prohibition (حرمت رضاعت) attaches if milk is dominant; it does not attach if medicine is dominant.
2
Locate the legal principle
The text states that consideration is given to the intended purpose (مقصود). When milk dominates, the purpose is nutrition (غذا); when medicine dominates, the purpose is treatment (تداوی).
3
Analyze the objection and response
An objection is raised: even a drop of milk should prohibit. The response is that the intended purpose overrides mere presence. Hence, if medicine is dominant, no prohibition, despite milk reaching the child.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
If a child drinks a mixture where medicine is clearly more than milk, and the goal is to cure an illness, no fosterage relationship is established. The milk is not the primary nutritional source.

Milk was mixed with medicine and the milk is dominant, then prohibition will attach.
And if it is mixed with medicine and the milk is dominant, prohibition attaches to it, because the milk remains intended in it, since the medicine is only to strengthen it to reach.

Explanation: If milk is mixed with medicine and the milk is dominant, then fosterage prohibition will be established. The evidence is that in obtaining nutrition, only milk is intended. The medicine is only for strengthening the milk's delivery. And if the milk is overwhelmed and the medicine is dominant, then prohibition is not established.
There is an objection on this: that if the medicine's role is only to give strength and nothing else, then whether the milk is dominant or overwhelmed, in both cases fosterage prohibition should be established. Because in the case of milk being overwhelmed, at least one drop will surely reach the child's throat, and one drop is also prohibited according to the Hanafis. The answer is that here consideration is of the intended purpose. So if the milk is dominant, then obtaining nutrition from it is intended, and the medicine is only for strength. And if the milk is overwhelmed, then the purpose is treatment, and the milk is to strengthen the medicine. After this difference is clear, no objection remains.

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when human milk is mixed with medicine. The key principle is that fosterage prohibition depends on the dominant component and the intended purpose.

If the milk is dominant in the mixture, prohibition attaches because the milk is the intended source of nutrition; the medicine merely facilitates its delivery. If the medicine is dominant, prohibition does not attach because the purpose is therapeutic (treatment), and the milk only serves to strengthen the medicine.

An objection is raised: since even a drop of milk creates prohibition, why should dominance matter? The answer is that the intended purpose changes: when milk is dominant, the goal is nutrition; when medicine is dominant, the goal is treatment. The Hanafi school looks at the intended purpose (مقصود), not merely the presence of milk.

This ruling is consistent with the overarching Hanafi principle of considering the dominant component and the underlying purpose in mixtures.

Key Terms
دواء (dawa'): Medicine; a substance used for treatment, mixed with milk
مقصود (maqsud): Intended purpose; the reason for which the mixture is administered
تداوی (tadawi): Treatment; the medical purpose for which the mixture is used

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The volume of milk present
B) The color of the mixture
C) The intended purpose and which component is dominant
D) The age of the child

Key Takeaway
Fosterage prohibition attaches only when milk is dominant and intended for nutrition, not when medicine is dominant and intended for treatment.

Dominance of Human Milk in Mixtures Determines Fosterage Prohibition
Ruling with proof via analogy to water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fosterage prohibition when human milk is mixed with animal milk and apply the principle of iʿtibār al-ghālib.

Core Idea
Only dominant human milk triggers fosterage prohibition; diluted milk does not.

This passage from al-Hidāyah addresses a nuance: when human milk (the only type that creates fosterage ties) is mixed with goat’s milk (which does not), which ruling prevails? The answer relies on a broader legal principle—the consideration of the dominant component (iʿtibār al-ghālib). Understanding this rule helps resolve similar mixed-substance questions in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mixture
Note that two substances are mixed: human milk (laban al-ādamiyyah) and goat's milk (laban al-sha'ah). Only human milk can establish fosterage prohibition (taḥrīm al-riḍā‘).
Animal milk never creates fosterage prohibition in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Determine the Relevant Ruling
The question is whether the mixture creates a fosterage relationship that prohibits marriage. The answer depends on which component dominates.
3
Apply the Principle of iʿtibār al-ghālib
The Ḥanafī legal maxim states that the ruling follows the dominant element in a mixture. Here, if human milk is dominant (ghālib), the mixture takes its ruling (prohibition attaches). If goat's milk is dominant, the mixture takes its ruling (no prohibition).
This principle is also applied to water mixed with milk or food.
4
Recognize the Proof (Qiyas)
The passage draws an analogy to water: just as a mixture of water and milk is treated as milk if milk is dominant, so too human milk and goat's milk follow the same logic. The common illa (effective cause) is the dominance of one substance.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) with a well-known asl.
5
State the Final Ruling
If human milk is dominant in the mixture, fosterage prohibition (taḥrīm) attaches. If goat's milk is dominant, no prohibition attaches. If equal, the default is no prohibition until evidence of dominance.
This is the muftā bihī position in the Ḥanafī school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا اختلط اللبن بلبن الشاة و هو الغالب تعلق به التحريم و ان غلب لبن الشاة لم يتعلق به التحريم اعتبارا للغالب كما في الماء
ترجمہ اور جب ( آدمیہ) کا دودھ بکری کے دودھ کے ساتھ مل گیا اور ( آدمیہ) کا دودھ غالب ہے تو اس کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق ہو گی۔ اور اگر بکری کا دودھ غالب ہے تو اس کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق نہیں ہوگی ۔ غالب کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے جیسا کہ پانی میں۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ اور دلیل دونوں واضح ہیں۔
And if the milk (of a human woman) mixes with the milk of a goat, and it (the human milk) is dominant, then prohibition attaches to it; and if the goat's milk is dominant, then prohibition does not attach to it, considering the dominant, as in water.
Translation: And when human milk mixes with goat's milk, and the human milk is dominant, then prohibition will attach to it. And if goat's milk is dominant, then prohibition will not attach to it, considering the dominant, as in water.
Explanation: The scenario and the evidence are both clear.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage provides a straightforward ruling: when human milk (which alone creates fosterage prohibition) is mixed with goat's milk (which does not create prohibition), the decisive factor is which is dominant. If the human milk is dominant, prohibition attaches; if the goat's milk is dominant, it does not. This is based on the principle of considering the dominant component (اعتبار غالب), analogous to the ruling when water is mixed with milk: if water is dominant, the mixture is treated as water, and vice versa.

The commentary notes that both the scenario and the evidence are clear, requiring no further elaboration. This ruling aligns with the earlier discussion on mixing with food and medicine, consistently applying the dominance principle.

Key Terms
لبن الشاة (laban al-sha'ah): Goat's milk; an animal milk that does not create fosterage prohibition
اعتبار الغالب (i'tibar al-ghalib): Considering the dominant; the principle that the ruling follows the dominant component in a mixture

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, because human milk is present
B) Only if the human milk is dominant in the mixture
C) Only if the goat's milk is dominant
D) Never, because goat's milk negates the effect of human milk

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, for a mixture of human and animal milk, fosterage prohibition attaches only when human milk is the dominant component.

Milk of Two Women Mixed: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fosterage Prohibition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mixed milk fosterage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on mixed milk fosterage, and explain the underlying reasoning about substance mixture.

Core Idea
Mixing same-genre milk: does it merge or remain distinct? The ruling on fosterage hangs on this.

When a child consumes milk that came from two different women, which woman becomes a foster mother? The answer depends on how the Hanafi imams view the mixture of like substances. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar, and the two narrations from Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Understand the scenario: two women's milk is mixed (in a container, etc.), then a child drinks it. Does fosterage prohibition attach to one, both, or none?
The issue arises from the mixture of two like (human) milks.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view and his reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds that prohibition attaches only to the woman whose milk is dominant. His reasoning: the mixture becomes one thing; the lesser portion is subordinate to the greater, so the ruling follows the dominant.
He applies the principle of subordination (taba'iyyah) of the lesser in same-genus mixtures.
3
State Muhammad and Zufar's view and their reasoning
Muhammad and Zufar hold that prohibition attaches to both women. Their reasoning: a thing does not become non-existent (mustahlik) when mixed with its own genus; each milk retains its legal identity, so both women become foster mothers.
They rely on the principle that same-genus mixtures do not cause loss of identity due to unity of purpose.
4
Note Abu Hanifa's two narrations
From Imam Abu Hanifa there are two narrations: one aligning with Abu Yusuf, one with Muhammad and Zufar. This shows the issue was debated within the school itself.
The text does not give a preferred narration; it refers to the chapter on oaths for further resolution.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf's view, only one woman becomes a foster mother (the dominant), so marriage to relatives of the other woman is permitted. Under Muhammad and Zufar, both become foster mothers, so marriage to relatives of both is prohibited.
This real-world difference makes the dispute practically significant.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the milk of two women mixes, prohibition attaches to the more dominant one according to Abu Yusuf, because all becomes one thing, so the less is made subordinate to the greater in building the ruling upon it. And Muhammad and Zufar said that prohibition attaches to both, because one genus does not overpower another genus; for a thing does not become non-existent when mixed with its genus, due to the unity of purpose. And from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations on this. The origin of this issue is in the chapter on oaths.
Translation: And when two women's milk is drunk, then prohibition attaches to the more dominant one according to Abu Yusuf. Because the whole becomes one thing, so the less is made subordinate to the greater in building the ruling. And Imam Muhammad and Zufar said that prohibition attaches to both. Because one genus does not overpower another genus. Because a thing does not become non-existent when mixed with its genus, due to the unity of purpose. And from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations on this. The origin of this issue is in the chapter on oaths.
Explanation: The scenario is that if milk of two women is mixed, then a child drinks it, will fosterage prohibition be established or not? There is a difference of opinion. Imam Abu Yusuf says that with whichever woman's milk is dominant, prohibition will be established with her. ...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the establishment of fosterage prohibition when the milk of two women is mixed and then consumed by a child.

Imam Abu Yusuf holds that prohibition attaches only to the woman whose milk is dominant in the mixture. His reasoning: when two similar substances mix, they become one entity, and the smaller portion is subordinate to the larger; thus the ruling follows the dominant.

Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Zufar hold that prohibition attaches to both women. Their reasoning: when a substance mixes with its own genus (here, human milk with human milk), one portion does not overpower the other; the milk of each remains legally distinct, so each woman becomes a foster mother. The unity of purpose (nutrition) does not erase individual identity.

From Imam Abu Hanifa, two narrations are reported: one agreeing with Abu Yusuf and one with Muhammad and Zufar. The text notes that the origin of this issue is in the chapter on oaths (الأيمان), where the same principle applies about mixtures of like substances.

This is a classic example of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where the ruling depends on the legal theory of mixtures (اختلاط الأجناس).

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus or kind; here it refers to the type of milk (human milk)
مستهلک (mustahlik): Becoming non-existent or fully absorbed; when a substance mixes with something of its own genus, it does not become mustahlik
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate; the component that is lesser in quantity and follows the ruling of the greater

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prohibition attaches only to the woman whose milk is dominant
B) Prohibition attaches to both women
C) No prohibition attaches to either woman
D) Prohibition attaches to both if the milk is not cooked

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when milk of two women mixes, there is an intra-school dispute: Abu Yusuf attaches prohibition only to the dominant milk, while Muhammad and Zufar attach it to both, based on different theories of mixture.

Man's Milk Does Not Create Fosterage Prohibition
Ruling on fosterage from a man's milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a man's milk does not create fosterage prohibition and explain the rational proof based on the nature of milk and childbirth.

Core Idea
A man's milk cannot create fosterage because it is not true milk—only milk enabling growth and development counts.

In this lesson, we examine a clear-cut ruling: a man's milk does not produce fosterage prohibition. The Hanafi school bases this on the definition of laban and the condition of growth. The passage provides a concise proof using qiyas: since men cannot give birth, their milk lacks the necessary nurturing quality. This is a ruling agreed upon by all four imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act under consideration? (A man's milk nursing a child.) What is the ruling? (No fosterage prohibition arises.)
The ruling is that the child does not become mahram.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a proof: the milk is not 'laban' in reality because it does not produce growth (nashw wa numuw). Growth is the essential effect of true milk.
This is a rational proof (ma'qul) based on the nature of milk.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection is that shariah terms for milk (laban) are tied to the capacity to cause growth, which is exclusive to females capable of childbirth (wiladah). Men lack this capacity, so their milk does not qualify.
This is a qiyas on female childbirth capacity.
4
Note the consensus
The passage indicates that the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree on this ruling, making it a settled issue.
No ikhtilaf exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا نزل للرجل لبن فارضع صبيا لم يتعلق به التحريم لانه ليس بلبن على التحقيق فلا يتعلق به النشو والنمو و هذا لان اللبن انما يتصور مما يتصور منه الولادة
And if a man's milk descends and he nurses a child, prohibition does not attach to it because it is not milk in reality, so growth and development do not attach to it. And this is because milk is only conceived from that from which childbirth is conceived.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage rules that a man's milk does not create fosterage prohibition. The reason is twofold: first, a man's milk is not considered true milk (laysa bi-laban 'ala al-tahqiq); second, the effective cause for prohibition is growth (nashw wa numuw), which is absent. The underlying principle is that milk (as a substance capable of nurturing) is only produced by those who can give birth—i.e., women. Since men cannot give birth, their milk lacks the quality that would support infant growth. This is a ruling upon which the four imams agree, as mentioned in the commentary.

Key Terms
لبن (laban): Milk that nourishes and causes growth; restricted to female milk in fosterage rulings.
ولادة (wilādah): Childbirth; the ability to give birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because man's milk is not true milk in the sense of fostering growth.
C) Yes, if the man is the child's father.
D) No, only if the milk is from a relative.

Key Takeaway
A man's milk does not create fosterage prohibition because it lacks the capacity to cause growth, being from one incapable of childbirth.

Adult Wife Nurses Minor Co-Wife: Marriage and Mahr
Ruling on marriage dissolution and mahr when fosterage occurs between co-wives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage dissolution and mahr when an adult wife nurses her minor co-wife, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement over reimbursement of the minor's mahr.

Core Idea
When an adult wife nurses the minor co-wife, both become haram; the adult forfeits her mahr, but the minor keeps half—and only intentional nursing requires the adult to reimburse.

This passage from Al-Hidayah tackles a unique scenario where fosterage accidentally corrupts a marriage. The ruling distinguishes between fault and mere causation, reflecting the Hanafi emphasis on intent in liability. We will unpack the legal consequences, the mahr obligations, and the intra-Hanafi dispute between Zahir al-Riwayah and Imam Muhammad regarding reimbursement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Immediate Consequence
The adult wife nurses the minor co-wife, creating a foster relationship: the adult becomes the minor's foster-mother, making the husband simultaneously married to a woman and her foster-daughter. This combination is prohibited like lineage, so both wives become haram immediately.
The prohibition is based on the general rule that one cannot marry a woman and her daughter, whether by blood or fosterage.
2
Determine the Mahr for Each Wife
The separation originates from the adult's action (nursing), so if the husband had not consummated with her, she gets no mahr because the divorce came from her side. The minor's separation was not from her side, so she is entitled to half the mahr (as in any non-consummated divorce).
Even though the minor participated in the nursing, her action is not considered as dropping her right, analogous to a legatee who kills the testator but unintentionally.
3
Analyze the Husband's Right to Recover from the Adult
The husband paid the minor's mahr and now recovers it from the adult if she intended to cause corruption. If she did not intend, she is not liable. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
The key distinction is intent: without it, the adult is only a cause, not a direct destroyer of the marriage.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Muhammad reports a contrary view: the husband recovers in both cases, whether intentional or not, because the adult caused the loss of the minor's mahr. The relied-upon position is the Zahir al-Riwayah, supported by qiyas to the case of a legatee killing the testator.
The dispute hinges on whether mere causation (tamaddud) suffices for liability or whether intent (niyya al-fasad) is required.
5
Understand the Reasoning via Qiyas
The Hanafi proof uses analogy to a legatee who kills the testator: if unintentional, the legatee does not lose inheritance; similarly, the adult's nursing is not inherently corruptive—it becomes so by circumstance (ittifaq al-hal). Thus, intent is necessary to impose liability.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that liability for destructive acts (itlaf) requires direct action, not mere secondary causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا تزوج الرجل صغيرة وكبيرة فارضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة حرمتا على الزوج لانه يصير جامعابين الام والبنت رضا عاوذلك حرام كالجمع بينها نسَباً ثم ان لم يدخل بالكبيرة فلا مهرلها لان الفرقة جأت من قبلها قبل الدخول بها وللصغيرة نصف المهرلان الفرقة وقعت لا من جهتها والارتضاع وان كان فعلامنها لكن فعلها غير معتبر فى اسقاط حقها كما اذاقتلت مورثها ويرجع به الزوج على الكبيرة ان كانت تعمدت به الفسادوان لم تتعمد فلا شيء عليها وان علمت بان الصغيرة امرأته وعن محمد انه يرجع في الوجهين والصحيح ظاهر الرواية لانها وان اكدت ماكان على شرف السقوط وهو نصف المهروذلك يجرى مجرى الاتلاف لكنها مسببة فيه امالان الارضاع ليس بافساد النكاح وضعا وانما يثبت ذلك باتفاق الحال
And if a man marries a minor and an adult, and the adult nurses the minor, both become forbidden to the husband because he becomes one who combines the mother and daughter through fosterage, and that is forbidden just like combining them by lineage. Then, if he has not consummated with the adult, there is no mahr for her because the separation came from her side before consummation with her. And for the minor, half the mahr because the separation occurred not from her side, even though the fostering was her action, but her action is not considered in dropping her right, just as if she killed her legator. And the husband recovers from the adult if she intended to cause corruption; but if she did not intend, there is nothing against her. And if she knew that the minor was his wife—and from Muhammad that he recovers in both cases. The correct position is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) because although she confirmed something that was on the verge of falling (half the mahr), and that is like destruction, yet she was a cause in it. But the fostering is not in law a corruption of the marriage; rather it is established by agreement of circumstances.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This complex passage deals with the case where a man marries two women: an adult and a minor. The adult then nurses the minor. This creates a foster-relationship: the adult becomes the foster-mother of the minor, and the minor becomes the foster-daughter of the adult. Since the husband is married to both, he becomes a foster-father to the minor (through the adult) and simultaneously husband to the adult. This results in the forbidden combination of a woman and her daughter (by fosterage), similar to the prohibition by lineage. Therefore, both wives become haram to him immediately. The passage then discusses the mahr consequences: if the husband had not consummated with the adult, she gets no mahr because the separation originated from her act (the nursing). The minor gets half the mahr because the separation is not from her side. The husband may recover the mahr he paid to the minor from the adult if she intentionally caused the corruption. There is an ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad says the husband recovers in both intentional and unintentional cases, but the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) differentiates based on intent, because the adult's act of nursing, though it caused the separation, is not inherently a corruption of the marriage—it only becomes so by circumstance. The analogy to killing the testator (who then loses inheritance) is used: mere causation without intent does not invalidate rights.

Key Terms
جامع بين الأم والبنت رضاعا (jāmiʿ bayn al-umm wal-bint riḍāʿan): Combining a woman and her foster-daughter in marriage; prohibited like blood relations.
فرقة (furqah): Separation/dissolution of marriage due to the fosterage relationship.
مهر (mahr): Dower; the obligatory payment from husband to wife upon marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (Zahir al-Riwayah) position, when does an adult wife who nurses her minor co-wife owe reimbursement to the husband for the minor's mahr?
A) Always, because she caused the separation.
B) Only if she intended to cause corruption.
C) Only if she knew the minor was his wife.
D) Never, because the husband is responsible.

Key Takeaway
Intent is crucial in Hanafi law: the adult wife is liable to reimburse the husband for the minor's mahr only if she intentionally nursed the minor to corrupt the marriage.

Drinking Goat's Milk Does Not Create Fosterage
Ruling on children drinking goat's milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fosterage through animal milk and explain why using the concept of juz'iyyah.

Core Idea
Only human milk creates fosterage; animal milk has no juz'iyyah.

This passage clarifies a key condition for fosterage (radā'): the milk must be human. Many assume any shared milk source creates milk kinship, but the Hanafi school restricts it to human milk based on the concept of juz'iyyah (partiality), which only applies between humans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is two children drinking from the same goat's milk. The ruling is that no fosterage prohibition is established between them.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the reason (ta'lil): 'because there is no juz'iyyah between humans and animals, and prohibition is on account of juz'iyyah.'
This is a rational argument based on the purpose of fosterage laws.
3
Understand the concept of juz'iyyah
Juz'iyyah means partiality or shared origin. It is the effective cause (illa) for the prohibition of marriage due to fosterage.
It is derived from the Qur'anic principle that foster mothers and sisters are prohibited (Qur'an 4:23).
4
Apply the principle
Since animal milk lacks juz'iyyah, it cannot create a legal relationship that prohibits marriage. Thus, the children are not foster-siblings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا اشرب صبيان من لبن شاة لم يتعلق به التحريم لانه لاجزئية بين الأدمى والبهائم والحرمة باعتبارها
And if two children drink from the milk of a goat, prohibition does not attach to it because there is no partiality between humans and animals, and prohibition is on account of partiality.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage rules that if two children (a boy and a girl) drink the milk of the same goat, no fosterage prohibition is established between them. The reason is that the concept of 'partiality' (juz'iyyah) only applies between humans. Fosterage creates a fictive kinship, which requires that the milk be from a human source. Animal milk does not create any familial relationship. The commentary mentions an interesting anecdote about Imam Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari, who apparently held the opposite view and was expelled from Bukhara for issuing a fatwa that goat's milk creates fosterage. The relied-upon Hanafi position, however, is clear: no prohibition.

Key Terms
جزئية (juz'iyyah): Partiality or shared origin; the basis for fosterage relationship between humans.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They become foster-siblings and cannot marry.
B) No fosterage relationship is established.
C) It is makruh for them to marry.
D) They become siblings only if the goat is owned by one of them.

Key Takeaway
Fosterage (radā') is only established through human milk because juz'iyyah is required, and animals lack this.

Man's Milk Does Not Create Fosterage Prohibition
States that man's milk and similar fluids do not create fosterage ties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that man's milk does not establish fosterage ties and explain the rational proof based on the definition of milk.

Core Idea
Only milk that causes growth establishes fosterage; man's milk is not true milk.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific question: does the milk of a man create fosterage ties? The answer is no, and the proof is rational. The author explains that milk can only be imagined from a person capable of childbirth, and since a man cannot give birth, his milk is not real milk. This lesson will clarify the ruling and its implications for similar cases like a virgin's fluid and a hermaphrodite's milk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is feeding a child with man's milk. The ruling is that fosterage prohibition (tahrim) is not established.
The same ruling applies to a virgin's yellowish fluid and a hermaphrodite's milk.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a rational analogy (qiyas): man's milk is not real milk, just as fish blood is not real blood.
The dalil is aqli (rational), not textual.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Milk is defined as a substance that comes from a childbearing person and causes growth. Man's milk does not cause growth, so it is not considered milk for legal purposes.
The essential attribute is the capacity for childbirth and nutritional growth.
4
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The ruling extends to any fluid that is not true milk: a virgin's colostrum-like fluid and a hermaphrodite's milk are treated the same.
All four imams agree on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Translation: And if a man's milk comes out, then he feeds it to a child, then prohibition will not be attached because of it. Because it is not really milk, so growth and development will not be associated with it. And this is because milk can be imagined from the person from whom childbirth can be imagined. Explanation: If milk comes out from a man's breast, and he feeds that milk to a child, then the prohibition of fosterage is not established (the four imams agree on this). The proof is that man's milk is not really milk, just as the blood of a fish is not really blood. Therefore, growth and development will not occur from it. And the fact that man's milk is not really milk is because milk can be imagined from the person from whom childbirth can be imagined. And since childbirth cannot be imagined from a man, therefore milk also cannot be imagined. And when milk cannot be imagined from a man, then prohibition will also not attach to it. Similarly, if a yellowish fluid comes out from a virgin's breast and she feeds it to a child, then the prohibition of fosterage is not established. In meaning, the milk of a hermaphrodite is in the ruling of a man's milk. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author of Al-Hidayah (via the Urdu commentary) states that the milk of a man, a virgin's colostrum-like fluid, and a hermaphrodite's milk do not establish fosterage prohibition. The core reason given is that true milk comes only from a person capable of childbirth (i.e., a woman who has reached puberty). Man's milk is not genuine milk; the author analogizes it to fish blood, which is not real blood. The four imams (Abu Hanifa, Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) agree on this. The proof is rational (dalil aqli): since milk's purpose is to nourish and cause growth, and man's milk does not cause growth, it is not considered milk for legal purposes. The same applies to a virgin's yellowish fluid (which is not true milk) and a hermaphrodite's milk (treated like man's milk). The Hanafi position is clear: only milk from a woman who can bear children creates fosterage ties.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage; the act of breastfeeding that creates legal prohibitions to marriage.
تحريم (tahrim): Prohibition, specifically the prohibition of marriage due to fosterage relationships.
لبن (laban): Milk, specifically human milk considered for fosterage rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quran explicitly exempts men's milk
D) Because the jurists disagreed and left no definitive ruling

Key Takeaway
Only milk from a childbearing woman creates fosterage ties; man's milk, virgin's colostrum, and hermaphrodite's milk do not.

Animal Milk and Fosterage: No Prohibition
Ruling with proof and historical expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing animal milk and explain why juz'iyyah is the basis for fosterage prohibition.

Core Idea
Animal milk does not create fosterage prohibition because human partiality (juz'iyyah) does not extend to animals.

Fosterage (rida') establishes a prohibition of marriage between the nursling and the suckler's relatives. However, not all milk is equal. In this lesson, we explore why sharing goat's or sheep's milk between children does not create any marital prohibition according to the Hanafi school, and why a contrary view was historically rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Two children drink from the same goat's milk. The ruling: no fosterage prohibition (hurmat) is established.
The act is permissible (mubah), but the legal effect on marriage is what matters.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites qiyas based on the phrase 'la juz'iyyah bain al-adami wa al-baha'im' (no partiality between humans and animals).
The dalil is indirect; it is an inference from the nature of fosterage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Fosterage prohibition is built on the concept of juz'iyyah (partial sharing of human nature). Since animals do not share this with humans, their milk does not create any kinship.
This is a meaning-based (illah) derivation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Bukhari (outside the Hanafi school) held that animal milk does create fosterage prohibition. The Hanafi school strongly rejects this.
The incident in Bukhara shows the practical consequence: Bukhari was expelled for his fatwa.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The established Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that animal milk does not create prohibition. The school maintains this based on the lack of juz'iyyah.
This is the view of Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

و اذا اشرب صبيان من لبن شاة لم يتعلق به التحريم لانه لاجزئية بين الأدمى والبهائم والحرمة باعتبارها ترجم - اور جب دو بچوں (لڑکا اور لڑکی ) نے ایک بکری کا دودھ پیا تو اس کے ساتھ تحریم متعلق نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ آدمی اور چوپائے کے درمیان کوئی جزئیت نہیں ہے۔ اور حرمت جزئیت ہی کے اعتبار سے ہوتی ہے۔

Two children drank a goat's milk; prohibition will not be attached. And if two children drink from the milk of a sheep, prohibition is not attached to it, because there is no partiality between humans and animals, and prohibition is based on partiality. Translation: And when two children (a boy and a girl) drank the milk of a goat, then prohibition will not be attached to it, because there is no partiality between humans and animals, and prohibition is based on partiality. Explanation: The case and proof are clear. However, consider an incident: Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari says that from this, the prohibition of fosterage will be established. Our Imam Bukhari came to Bukhara during the time of Sheikh Abu Hafs al-Kabir and started giving fatwas. The Sheikh told him not to do this, but Imam Bukhari avoided accepting the Sheikh's advice. Finally, once a public question was asked: if two children drink a goat's milk, what is the ruling? The Imam gave a fatwa establishing prohibition. After that, people gathered and Imam Bukhari was expelled from Bukhara because of this fatwa. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling that sharing animal milk (like goat's or sheep's milk) between children does not create fosterage prohibition. The proof is that there is no partiality (juz'iyyah) between humans and animals; complete fosterage ties exist only among humans. The Hidayah text states this clearly. The commentary then relates a historical incident involving Imam Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari (the famous muhaddith), who reportedly held the opposite view—that sharing animal milk does create fosterage prohibition. The story shows that Imam Bukhari was expelled from Bukhara for issuing such a fatwa against the established Hanafi position. The Hanafi school firmly rejects this view, as animal milk does not cause growth in the same way human milk does, and the legal basis for fosterage (being considered part of the family) does not apply to animals.

Key Terms
جزئية (juz'iyyah): Partiality or share; the concept that humans share a common nature or kinship that makes fosterage meaningful.
حرمة رضاع (hurmat rada'): The prohibition of marriage arising from fosterage relationships.

D) Because the Prophet forbade considering animal milk for fosterage

Key Takeaway
Animal milk, unlike human milk, does not create fosterage prohibition because there is no partiality (juz'iyyah) between humans and animals.

Major Nurses Minor: Prohibition and Mahr Liability
Intra-Hanafi dispute over mahr recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mahr consequences when a major wife nurses her minor co-wife, and identify the condition for the husband to reclaim half the mahr.

Core Idea
Intent matters: husband reclaims half mahr from major wife only if she intended to break the marriage.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced case where a major wife nurses her minor co-wife, triggering permanent prohibition for the husband. The ruling on mahr involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: under what conditions can the husband reclaim the half mahr he owes to the minor? The relied-upon position ties liability to the major's intent, illustrating the Hanafi principle that indirect causation (sababiyyah) requires transgression (ta'addi).

Guided Path
1
State the main ruling on prohibition
Identify that both wives become permanently prohibited to the husband because the nursing creates a fosterage relationship making them mother and daughter in relation to him.
This applies even if the major did not intend prohibition.
2
Determine the mahr for each wife
If no consummation, the major gets no mahr (separation from her side), the minor gets half mahr (separation not from her side). The husband pays half mahr to the minor.
Minor's right to half mahr is established regardless of her intent.
3
Identify the dispute over reclaiming half mahr
The husband may reclaim the half mahr from the major. The dispute: can he reclaim in all cases (Nawadir) or only if she intended to break the marriage (Zahir al-Riwayah)?
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and the relied-upon view.
4
Analyze the reasoning for the relied-upon view
The major is a sabab (indirect cause). Liability for indirect causes requires ta'addi (transgression), which requires knowledge of the marriage and intent to cause separation. Nursing without intent is not transgressive.
Analogy: digging a well only incurs liability if negligent.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Test: if the major nurses to save the minor from starving, knowing she is married, she is not liable because her intent was mercy, not corruption.
This distinguishes intent from mere knowledge.

Source Text

ایک آدمی نے صغیرہ اور کبیرہ سے نکاح کیا کبیرہ نے صغیرہ کو دودھ پلایا، دونوں حرام ہو جائیں گی
و اذا تزوج الرجل صغيرة وكبيرة فارضعت الكبيرة الصغيرة حرمتا على الزوج لانه يصير جامعابين الام والبنت رضا عاوذلك حرام كالجمع بينها نسَباً ثم ان لم يدخل بالكبيرة فلا مهرلها لان الفرقة جأت من قبلها قبل الدخول بها وللصغيرة نصف المهرلان الفرقة وقعت لا من جهتها والارتضاع وان كان فعلامنها لكن فعلها غير معتبر فى اسقاط حقها كما اذاقتلت مورثها ويرجع به الزوج على الكبيرة ان كانت تعمدت به الفسادوان لم تتعمد فلا شيء عليها وعن محمد انه يرجع في الوجهين والصحيح ظاهر الرواية لانها وان اكدت ماكان على شرف السقوط وهو نصف المهروذلك يجرى مجرى الاتلاف لكنها مسببة فيه امالان الارضاع ليس بافساد النكاح وضعا وانما يثبت ذلك باتفاق الحال
اولان فساد النكاح ليس بسبب لالزام المهربل هو سبب لسقوطه الا ان نصف المهريجب بطريق المتعة على ماعرف لكن من شرطه ابطال النكاح واذا كانت مسببة يشترط فيه التعدى كحفر البير ثم انما تكون متعدية اذا علمت بالنكاح وقصدت بالارضاع الفساد اما اذالم تعلم بالنكاح او علمت بالنكاح ولكنها قصدت دفع الجوع والهلاك من الصغيرة دون الافساد لا تكون متعدية لانها مامورة بذلك ولو علمت بالنكاح ولم تعلم بالفساد لا تكون متعدية ايضا وهذا منا اعتبار الجهل لدفع قصد الفساد لالدفع الحكم
ترجمہ اور جب کسی مرد نے ایک صغیرہ ( دودھ پیتی بچی) اور ایک کبیرہ سے نکاح کر لیا۔ پھر اس کبیرہ نے صغیرہ کو ( ہدتِ رضاعت میں دودھ پلا دیا تو شوہر پر دونوں حرام ہو جائیں گی۔ کیونکہ یہ (مرد) رضاعی ماں اور بیٹی کو جمع کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اور یہ حرام ہے۔ جیسا کہ نسبی ماں اور بیٹی کو جمع کرنا ( حرام) ہے۔ پھر اگر کبیرہ کیساتھ دخول نہیں ہوا تو اس کیلئے مہر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فرقبت اسی کی جانب سے آئی ہے اس کے ساتھ دخول کرنے سے پہلے ۔ اور صغیرہ کیلئے نصف مہر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فرقت اس کی جانب سے واقع نہیں ہوئی۔ اور دودھ چوسنا اگر چہ اس کا فعل ہے لیکن اس کا فعل اس کے حق ساقط کرنے میں معتبر نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ جب صغیرہ نے اپنے مورث کو قتل کر ڈالا ۔ اور شوہر کبیرہ سے نصف مہر رجوع کرلے گا اگر کبیرہ نے اس سے فساد (نکاح) کا ارادہ کیا ہو۔ اور اگر ارادہ نہیں کیا ( فساد نکاح) کا تو کبیرہ پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ جانتی ہے کہ صغیرہ اس کی بیوی ہے ( یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے )۔ اور ( نوادر میں ) امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ (شوہر) دونوں صورتوں میں رجوع کرے گا۔ (فساد کا ارادہ ہو یا نہ ہو ) اور صحیح ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ کیونکہ کبیرہ نے اگر چہ ( ایسا مال) مؤکد کر دیا جو ساقط ہونے کے قریب تھا اور وہ نصف مہر ہے۔ اور یہ ( تاکید مہر ) تلف کرنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ لیکن کبیرہ اس فعل میں مسببہ ہے یا تو اسلئے کہ دودھ پلانا فساد نکاح کیلئے موضوع نہیں ہے۔ اور پر (فساد نکاح) اتفاقاً ثابت ہو گیا۔ یا اسلئے کہ فساد نکاح الزام مہر کا سبب نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ سقوط مہر کا سبب ہے مگر یہ کہ نصف مہر بطور متعہ کے واجب ہوتا ہے چنانچہ معلوم ہوا لیکن اس کے وجوب کی شرط نکاح کا باطل ہونا ہے۔ اور جب ( کبیرہ) مسبہ ہے تو اس میں تعدی کی شرط ہو گی ۔ جیسے کنواں کھودنا، پھر ( کبیرہ) متعدیہ اس وقت ہوگی جبکہ (اس کو ) نکاح کا علم ہو اور دودھ پلانے سے فساد (نکاح) کا ارادہ کیا ہو۔ بہر حال جب (اس کو ) نکاح کا علم نہیں ہے یا نکاح تو معلوم ہے۔ لیکن اس نے صغیرہ سے بھوک اور ہلاکت دفع کرنے کا اعادہ کیا ہے نہ کہ (نکاح) فاسد کرنے کا۔ تو یہ کبیرہ) متعدیہ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ( کبیرہ) ایسا ( کرنے کی شرعا ) مامور ہے۔ اور اگر نکاح کا علم ہے اور فساد ( نکاح ) نہیں جانتی تب بھی متعد یہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور یہ جہل کا اعتبار ہماری طرف سے فساد کے ارادہ کو دفع کرنے کیلئے ہے نہ کہ حکم ( شرع) کو دفع کرنے کیلئے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے نکاح میں ایک کبیرہ ہے اور ایک دودھ پیتی بچی ۔ کبیرہ عورت نے اس صغیرہ رضعیہ کو اپنا دودھ پلا دیا تو اس شوہر پر یہ دونوں حرام ہو جائیں گی۔ اسی کے قائل امام شافعی اور امام احمد ہیں۔ کبیرہ کی حرمت موبدہ تو اسلئے ہے کہ وہ اپنے شوہر کی رضاعی ساس ہو گئی ۔ اور صغیرہ کے بارے میں قدرے تفصیل ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر اس شوہر نے کبیرہ کے ساتھ وطی کی تھی اس کے نتیجہ میں اس کبیرہ سے بچہ پیدا ہوا اور دودھ اتر آیا پھر کبیرہ نے یہ دودھ اس کی صغیرہ رضعیہ بیوی کو پلا دیا تو اس صغیرہ کے ساتھ بھی حرمت موبدہ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اسلئے کہ یہ صغیرہ اس کی رضاعی بیٹی ہوگئی۔ اور یہ شوہر اس کا رضاعی باپ ہو گیا۔
A man married a minor and a major; the major nursed the minor; both become prohibited for the husband. And if a man marries a minor and a major, and the major nurses the minor, both become prohibited for the husband, because he becomes one who combines a mother and daughter by fosterage, and that is unlawful, just like combining them by lineage. Then if he has not consummated with the major, she gets no mahr because the separation came from her side before consummation. The minor gets half the mahr because the separation did not occur from her side. Even though nursing is her act, her act is not considered in dropping her right, just as when she killed her inheritor. The husband will claim the half mahr from the major if she intended the corruption. If she did not intend it, nothing is on her. From Muhammad it is narrated that he claims in both cases; the correct is the apparent narration. Because she though confirmed what was on the verge of falling, that is half the mahr, and that takes the place of destruction, but she is causative in it, because nursing is not a cause for corrupting the marriage in principle, rather that is established incidentally. Or because corruption of marriage is not a cause for imposing mahr, rather it is a cause for dropping it, except that half mahr is due by way of mut'ah, as is known, but its condition is the invalidation of the marriage. When she is causative, transgression is a condition, like digging a well. Then she is transgressive only if she knew of the marriage and intended corruption by nursing. If she did not know of the marriage, or knew but intended to ward off hunger and destruction from the minor without corruption, she is not transgressive because she is commanded to do that. Even if she knew of the marriage and did not know of the corruption, she is not transgressive. This is consideration of ignorance to ward off the intention of corruption, not to ward off the ruling. Explanation: The case is that a man has a major and a nursing minor in his marriage. The major woman nursed the minor with her milk, then both become prohibited for this husband. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. The permanent prohibition of the major is because she becomes the fosterage mother-in-law of her husband. For the minor there is some detail: if the husband had intercourse with the major, resulting in a child, and her milk came out, then she feeds that milk to his minor wife, then the minor also becomes permanently prohibited, because she became his fosterage daughter and he became her fosterage father.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed case from Al-Hidayah: a man marries a major woman and a minor infant girl. The major nurses the minor. As a result, both wives become permanently prohibited to the husband. The reason is that by nursing, the major becomes the husband's fosterage mother-in-law (since she nursed his wife), and the minor becomes his fosterage daughter (if the milk came from the husband's own child with the major). The text then discusses the mahr (dower) implications. If the husband has not consummated the marriage with the major, she gets no mahr because the separation (due to prohibition) came from her side (she caused it by nursing). The minor, however, gets half the mahr because the separation did not arise from her act. The husband can recover that half mahr from the major if she intended to break the marriage. If she did not intend it (e.g., she nursed out of necessity), she is not liable. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (in Nawadir) holds that the husband can reclaim the half mahr from the major in both cases (whether she intended or not), but the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that he can only reclaim if she intended corruption. The commentary explains the reasoning: the major is a sabab (cause) but not a direct agent of the dissolution; she is considered 'mubasharah' (direct) only if she intended harm. Analogy is made to digging a well: one is liable only if negligent. The text also notes that the prohibition is agreed upon by the three main schools (Hanafi, Shafi'i, Hanbali).

Key Terms
مسبب (musabbib): An indirect cause; one who sets in motion a chain of events leading to a result, as opposed to direct agent (mubashir).
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression or wrongful conduct; acting beyond one's right.
فرقة (furqa): Separation; in this context, the dissolution of the marriage due to fosterage prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in the Hidayah, when can the husband reclaim the half mahr from the major wife after she nurses the minor wife?
A) In all cases, regardless of her intent
B) Only if she knew the minor was his wife and intended to break the marriage
C) Only if she did not know the minor was his wife
D) Only if she consulted the husband first

Key Takeaway
The husband reclaims half mahr from the major wife only when she intended to break the marriage, because indirect causation requires active transgression.

Nikah — Marriage

Mahr for the Adult Wife and Husband's Recovery
Ruling on adult's mahr and husband's recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mahr consequence for the adult wife when her breastfeeding dissolves the marriage and identify the condition under which the husband recovers half mahr from her.

Core Idea
The adult loses mahr because separation is from her side; the husband recovers half mahr only if she intended dissolution.

This lesson examines the financial consequences for an adult wife who breastfeeds her minor co-wife, causing both marriages to dissolve. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between the adult's mahr (which drops) and the husband's right to recover half the mahr he paid to the minor. The key factor is the adult's intention—whether she acted with ta'addi (transgression) or not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal situation
A man marries an adult and a minor; the adult breastfeeds the minor, making both women forbidden to him. Determine the ruling on the adult's mahr before consummation.
2
Analyze why the adult loses mahr
The separation (furqah) before consummation is attributed to the adult's action of breastfeeding. Since it came from her side, her mahr drops entirely.
This applies even if she did not intend dissolution—the act itself causes separation from her side.
3
Understand the husband's right of recovery
The husband pays half mahr to the minor. He can recover this amount from the adult only if she intended to dissolve the marriage (ta'addi). If she was unaware, forced, or acting out of necessity, she is not liable.
Zahir al-Riwayah holds this condition; Imam Muhammad in Nawadir says recovery in all cases, but the relied-upon position is the former.
4
Distinguish mutasabbibah from mubashirah
The adult is a mutasabbibah (indirect cause). Liability for indirect causation requires transgression (ta'addi). She is only a transgressor if she knew the marriage and intended to dissolve it. If she intended to save the child's life or was ignorant, she is not liable.
The analogy of digging a well is used: a well-digger is liable only if he transgresses.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم کتاب الرضاع

اور جب کسی مرد نے ایک صغیرہ ( دودھ پیتی بچی) اور ایک کبیرہ سے نکاح کر لیا۔ پھر اس کبیرہ نے صغیرہ کو ( مدتِ رضاعت میں دودھ پلا دیا تو شوہر پر دونوں حرام ہو جائیں گی۔ کیونکہ یہ (مرد) رضاعی ماں اور بیٹی کو جمع کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اور یہ حرام ہے۔ جیسا کہ نسبی ماں اور بیٹی کو جمع کرنا ( حرام) ہے۔

پھر اگر کبیرہ کے ساتھ دخول نہیں ہوا تو اس کے لیے مہر نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فرقت اسی کی جانب سے آئی ہے اس کے ساتھ دخول کرنے سے پہلے۔ اور صغیرہ کے لیے نصف مہر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فرقت اس کی جانب سے واقع نہیں ہوئی۔ اور دودھ چوسنا اگر چہ اس کا فعل ہے لیکن اس کا فعل اس کے حق ساقط کرنے میں معتبر نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ جب صغیرہ نے اپنے مورث کو قتل کر ڈالا۔

اور شوہر کبیرہ سے نصف مہر رجوع کرلے گا اگر کبیرہ نے اس سے فساد (نکاح) کا ارادہ کیا ہو۔ اور اگر ارادہ نہیں کیا ( فساد نکاح) کا تو کبیرہ پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ جانتی ہے کہ صغیرہ اس کی بیوی ہے ( یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے )۔

اور ( نوادر میں ) امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ (شوہر) دونوں صورتوں میں رجوع کرے گا۔ (فساد کا ارادہ ہو یا نہ ہو ) اور صحیح ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ کیونکہ کبیرہ نے اگر چہ ( ایسا مال) مؤکد کر دیا جو ساقط ہونے کے قریب تھا اور وہ نصف مہر ہے۔ اور یہ ( تاکید مہر ) تلف کرنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ لیکن کبیرہ اس فعل میں مسببہ ہے یا تو اس لیے کہ دودھ پلانا فساد نکاح کے لیے موضوع نہیں ہے۔ اور پر (فساد نکاح) اتفاقاً ثابت ہو گیا۔ یا اس لیے کہ فساد نکاح الزام مہر کا سبب نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ سقوط مہر کا سبب ہے مگر یہ کہ نصف مہر بطور متعہ کے واجب ہوتا ہے چنانچہ معلوم ہوا لیکن اس کے وجوب کی شرط نکاح کا باطل ہونا ہے۔

اور جب ( کبیرہ) مسببہ ہے تو اس میں تعدی کی شرط ہو گی۔ جیسے کنواں کھودنا، پھر ( کبیرہ) متعدیہ اس وقت ہوگی جبکہ (اس کو ) نکاح کا علم ہو اور دودھ پلانے سے فساد (نکاح) کا ارادہ کیا ہو۔ بہر حال جب (اس کو ) نکاح کا علم نہیں ہے یا نکاح تو معلوم ہے۔ لیکن اس نے صغیرہ سے بھوک اور ہلاکت دفع کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے نہ کہ (نکاح) فاسد کرنے کا۔ تو یہ (کبیرہ) متعدیہ نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ( کبیرہ) ایسا ( کرنے کی شرعا ) مامور ہے۔ اور اگر نکاح کا علم ہے اور فساد ( نکاح ) نہیں جانتی تب بھی متعدیہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور یہ جہل کا اعتبار ہماری طرف سے فساد کے ارادہ کو دفع کرنے کے لیے ہے نہ کہ حکم ( شرع) کو دفع کرنے کے لیے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کے نکاح میں ایک کبیرہ ہے اور ایک دودھ پیتی بچی۔ کبیرہ عورت نے اس صغیرہ رضعیہ کو اپنا دودھ پلا دیا تو اس شوہر پر یہ دونوں حرام ہو جائیں گی۔ اسی کے قائل امام شافعی اور امام احمد ہیں۔ کبیرہ کی حرمت مؤبّدہ تو اس لیے ہے کہ وہ اپنے شوہر کی رضاعی ساس ہو گئی۔ اور صغیرہ کے بارے میں قدرے تفصیل ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر اس شوہر نے کبیرہ کے ساتھ وطی کی تھی اس کے نتیجہ میں اس کبیرہ سے بچہ پیدا ہوا اور دودھ اتر آیا پھر کبیرہ نے یہ دودھ اس کی صغیرہ رضعیہ بیوی کو پلا دیا تو اس صغیرہ کے ساتھ بھی حرمت مؤبّدہ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اس لیے کہ یہ صغیرہ اس کی رضاعی بیٹی ہوگئی۔ اور یہ شوہر اس کا رضاعی باپ ہو گیا۔ اور اگر اس کبیرہ کا دودھ پہلے شوہر سے اترا اور اس شخص نے پہلے شوہر کے طلاق دینے کے بعد اس سے نکاح کیا درآنحالیکہ یہ کبیرہ دودھ والی ہے۔ پھر اس کبیرہ نے اس کی صغیرہ بیوی کو دودھ پلا دیا تو اب دیکھنا ہے کہ یہ شوہر ثانی اس کبیرہ کے ساتھ دخول کر چکا یا نہیں۔ اگر دخول کر چکا ہے تب بھی صغیرہ کے ساتھ حرمت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر کبیرہ کے ساتھ دخول نہیں ہوا تو صغیرہ اس شوہر پر حرام نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ صغیرہ ربائبہ ہے۔ اور ربائبہ کا یہی حکم ہے کہ اگر اس کی ماں کے ساتھ دخول ہو چکا تو ربائبہ سے نکاح حرام ہے۔ اور اگر اس کی ماں سے دخول نہیں ہوا تو نکاح حلال ہے۔ (فتح القدیر، الکفایہ)

بہر حال کبیرہ اور صغیرہ دونوں کے حرام ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں رضاعی ماں بیٹی ہوگئی ہیں اور رضاعی ماں بیٹی کا نکاح میں جمع کرنا اسی طرح حرام ہے جیسا کہ نسبی ماں بیٹی کا جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔

ثم أن لم يدخل بالكبيرة سے مہر کا حکم بیان فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر شوہر نے کبیرہ کے ساتھ دخول نہیں کیا ہے تو شوہر پر کبیرہ کے لیے مہر واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ دودھ پلانے سے فساد نکاح کا ارادہ کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ کبیرہ کے دودھ پلانے کی وجہ سے فرقت قبل الدخول اسی کی جانب سے آئی ہے۔ اور قبل الدخول عورت کی جانب سے فرقت کا واقع ہونا نصف مہر کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کبیرہ کے لیے مہر واجب نہیں ہوگا۔

چونکہ سقوط مہر کی علت کبیرہ کی جانب فرقت کو منسوب کرنا ہے۔ اس لیے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اگر دودھ پلانے کے لیے کبیرہ پر جبر کیا گیا یا وہ سوئی ہوئی تھی صغیرہ نے خود بخود منہ لگا کر دودھ پی لیا یا کسی شخص نے کبیرہ کا دودھ لے کر اس صغیرہ کے منہ میں ڈال دیا یا کبیرہ نے دیوانگی کی حالت میں دودھ پلا دیا تو ان تمام صورتوں میں کبیرہ کے لیے نصف مہر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ان صورتوں میں کبیرہ کی جانب فرقت کو منسوب نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے۔

اور اگر شوہر اس کبیرہ کے ساتھ دخول کر چکا تو اس کے لیے پورا مہر واجب ہو گا۔ البتہ شوہر پر عدت کا نفقہ واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ جنایت کبیرہ ہی کی طرف سے ہے۔

رہی یہ بات کہ صغیرہ کے لیے مہر ہو گا یا نہیں۔ سو اس بارے میں احناف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کے لیے نصف مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فرقت صغیرہ کی جانب سے بھی واقع ہوئی ہے۔ بایں طور کہ وہ کبیرہ کی بیٹی بن گئی۔ پس جس طرح کبیرہ کا مہر ساقط ہو گیا اسی طرح اس کا بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔

احناف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ کی جانب سے فرقت واقع نہیں ہوئی لیکن اگر آپ اشکال کریں کہ دودھ پینا تو صغیرہ کا فعل ہے لہذا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ صغیرہ کی جانب سے فرقت پائی گئی۔ تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ دودھ پینا اگر چہ صغیرہ کا فعل ہے۔ اور فساد نکاح اس سے واقع ہوا ہے لیکن صغیرہ کا فعل اس کے حق کو ساقط کرنے میں شرعا معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ صغیرہ احکام شرع کی مخاطب نہیں۔ اس وجہ سے اس کے کسی فعل پر شریعت کا حکم مرتب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ صغیرہ نے اپنے کسی مورث کو قتل کر ڈالا تو وہ غیر منقول کی وارث ہوگی۔ اور اس کا قتل شرعاً حرمان وراثت کا موجب نہیں ہو گا۔ درآنحالیکہ قاتل اپنے مورث مقتول کی وراثت سے محروم کر دیا جاتا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شریعت نے صغیرہ کے فعل قتل کا اعتبار نہیں کیا ہے۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ طبعا دودھ پینے پر مجبور ہے۔ اور کبیرہ اپنا پستان اس کے منہ میں ڈالنے کے سلسلہ میں مختار ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ افعال مختار کی طرف منسوب کئے جاتے ہیں نہ کہ مجبور کی طرف۔ (صغیرہ کے قتل کرنے کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ صغیرہ چھت پر ہے اور ماں نیچے سو رہی ہے۔ پس صغیرہ نے ایک پتھر اوپر سے نیچے اپنی ماں پر گرادیا جس کے نتیجہ میں موت واقع ہوگئی)۔

(الکفایہ) مصنف ويرجع الزوج سے یہ حکم بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ جو نصف مہر صغیرہ کو دیا ہے شوہر اس کو کبیرہ سے واپس لینے کا مجاز ہے یا۔
When a man marries a minor (suckling girl) and an adult woman, then the adult breastfeeds the minor within the breastfeeding period, then both become forbidden to the husband, because he is collecting a foster mother and daughter, and that is forbidden, just as collecting a biological mother and daughter is forbidden. If he had not consummated with the adult, no mahr is due to her, because the separation came from her side before consummation. For the minor, half mahr is due, because separation did not occur from her side. Her drinking of milk, even though it is her action, is not legally considered to drop her right, like when a minor kills her relative (she still inherits). The husband will recover half mahr from the adult if she intended to cause dissolution; if she did not intend, nothing is due from her, even if she knew the minor is his wife (this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah). In Nawadir, Imam Muhammad narrates that the husband recovers in both cases (whether she intended or not). The correct position is Zahir al-Riwayah, because the adult, although she made a debt (mahr) that was about to fall, is a mere cause (mutasabbibah) in this act. For a cause, transgression is required, like digging a well. She becomes a transgressor only if she knew of the marriage and intended dissolution. If she did not know of the marriage, or knew but intended to satisfy the minor's hunger rather than dissolve the marriage, she is not a transgressor because she is commanded (to feed). Even if she knew of the marriage but did not know it would cause dissolution, she is not a transgressor. This consideration of ignorance is from us to negate the intention of dissolution, not to negate the divine ruling. The detailed scenario: a man has in his marriage an adult and a minor girl. The adult breastfeeds the minor, so both become forbidden—Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad agree. The adult becomes the husband's foster mother-in-law; regarding the minor, if the husband had intercourse with the adult resulting in a child and milk, then the minor becomes a foster daughter. If the milk was from a previous husband, then after divorce the man marries the adult while she has milk; if he then consumes the marriage, the minor becomes forbidden; if he did not consume, the minor is not forbidden, as she is a stepdaughter (rabibah) and the rule for stepdaughters is that if he has consummated with the mother, the stepdaughter is forbidden; otherwise, she is permissible. The reason for prohibition is that they become foster mother and daughter, and collecting them in marriage is like collecting biological mother and daughter. Then the text explains the ruling on mahr: if the husband did not consummate with the adult, no mahr is due to her, regardless of her intention, because the separation before consummation came from her side, and separation from the woman's side before consummation drops half mahr. Therefore no mahr is due. However, if she was forced, or sleeping, or the minor drank on her own, or someone else fed, or she was insane, then half mahr is due to her because separation cannot be attributed to her. If he had consummated with her, full mahr is due, but no 'iddah maintenance, because the transgression is from her side. Regarding the minor, the Hanafis say half mahr is due. Imam Malik says it is not due, arguing that separation also occurred from her side as she became the adult's daughter. The Hanafi proof: separation did not occur from the minor's side. If one objects that drinking is her action so separation is from her, we respond that her action is not legally considered to drop her right because she is not addressed by the Shariah. This is like a minor killing her relative: she still inherits, even though a killer is barred. That shows the Shariah does not consider the minor's action. Second proof: the minor is naturally compelled to drink, while the adult is free in putting her breast in the mouth. The rule is: actions are attributed to the free agent, not to the compelled. The author then says the husband recovers the half mahr he paid to the minor from the adult.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling (with proof) from the Hanafi school on the mahr consequences when an adult wife breastfeeds a minor co-wife, causing immediate dissolution of both marriages due to fosterage prohibitions. The commentary explains that the adult woman loses her mahr entirely if the marriage was not consummated, because the separation (furqah) is attributed to her action (breastfeeding). The minor, however, retains half mahr because her action (drinking) is not legally attributable to her—she is not a mukallafah. The husband may recover the half mahr from the adult wife only if she intentionally caused the dissolution (Zahir al-Riwayah); Imam Muhammad's contrary view in Nawadir is not relied upon. The passage also addresses scenarios where the adult is not a transgressor (e.g., she was forced or unaware), in which case she keeps half mahr. Inter-madhhab disputes are noted: Imam Malik holds that the minor also loses mahr (opposing the Hanafi view), and Imam Shafi'i and Ahmad agree on the prohibition but with different details regarding the minor's status depending on consummation with the adult. The Hanafi proof uses qiyas: just as a minor who kills a relative is not barred from inheritance, so too a minor's breastfeeding does not nullify her right to mahr. The passage is an expansion of the Hidayah's matn, typical of the sharh style of Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
مسببہ (mutasabbibah): A person who causes an outcome indirectly, not directly as a direct agent (mubashirah).
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or fault that makes an indirect cause liable.
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage through breastfeeding that creates permanent marriage prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah), when does the husband recover half mahr from the adult wife who caused dissolution by breastfeeding?
A) In all cases, because she caused the dissolution
B) Only if she intended to cause the dissolution
C) Only if she knew the minor was his wife
D) Only if she did not know the minor was his wife

Key Takeaway
The adult wife loses her mahr, but the husband recovers half mahr from her only if she intended to dissolve the marriage.
