Evidence for Fosterage: Hanafi vs Maliki vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on witness numbers for fosterage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires two men or one man and two women to prove fosterage, and evaluate the Maliki and Shafi'i counter-arguments using the concept of inseparability of prohibition from dissolution of marriage.

Core Idea
In fosterage, prohibition is inseparable from marriage dissolution, so evidence must match marriage dissolution's witness requirements.

Fosterage (rada') creates a permanent marriage prohibition. How many witnesses are needed to prove it? The Hanafi, Maliki, and Shafi'i schools disagree. This lesson dissects each school's reasoning, focusing on the Hanafi argument that the nature of the prohibition dictates the standard of proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: fosterage is proven by two men or one man and two women; women alone are insufficient. Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
The Hanafi position is based on the connection between fosterage prohibition and dissolution of marriage.
2
Identify opposing schools and their views
Malik: one just woman suffices. Shafi'i: four women are required. Understand their basic claims before examining proofs.
Malik treats fosterage as a purely religious matter; Shafi'i focuses on the private nature of the act.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Malik analogizes to meat: a single report of impermissibility suffices. Shafi'i argues that men cannot witness the act, so four women stand in for two men.
Both opponents use analogical reasoning (qiyas) but differ in the underlying 'illa.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes both analogies. Against Malik: meat prohibition can coexist with ownership, but fosterage prohibition is permanent and terminates marriage. Against Shafi'i: men can witness fosterage through mahram relatives, so the privacy argument fails.
The key distinction is the inseparability of prohibition from dissolution of ownership in marriage (zawal al-milk).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi, a fosterage claim requires testimony of two men or one man and two women; under Maliki, one woman suffices; under Shafi'i, four women are needed.
This affects court procedures in different jurisdictions following different schools.

سکتا۔ اور جن چیزوں پر مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتا ہے، ان چیزوں میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک چار عورتوں کی گواہی شرط ہے تا کہ دو عورتیں ایک مرد کے قائم مقام ہو جائیں۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ رضاعت ان چیزوں میں سے نہیں ہے جن پر مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ بلکہ حقیقت یہ ہے کہ رضاعت پر مرد مطلع ہو سکتے ہیں۔ مثلاً ذوی الارحام کا اس کے پستان کی طرف دیکھنا حلال ہے۔ لہذا یہ دلیل قابل قبول نہ ہوگی۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرمت حقوق شرع میں سے ایک حق ہے اور حقوق شرع امور دینیہ ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا حرمت بھی امر دینی ہوئی اور امر دینی ایک آدمی کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ (وہ ایک آدمی مرد ہو یا عورت بشرطیکہ عادل ہو ) مثلاً ایک شخص نے گوشت خریدا پھر ایک آدمی نے مشتری کو خبر دی کہ یہ گوشت آتش پرست کا ذبیحہ ہے تو اس مشتری پر یہ گوشت حرام ہو گیا۔ نہ کھا سکتا ہے اور نہ دوسروں کو کھلا سکتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ امور دینیہ کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے ایک آدمی کی شہادت کافی ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باب نکاح میں ثبوت حرمت زوال ملک سے جدا نہیں ہوتی ۔ یعنی یہ نہیں ہوسکتا کہ رضاعت کی وجہ سے حرمت نکاح ثابت ہو جائے۔ اور ملک نکاح باقی رہے۔ کیونکہ حرمت موبد کے ساتھ بقاء نکاح ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پس جب رضاعت کی وجہ سے حرمت ثابت ہو گی تو نکاح بھی باطل ہوگا۔ اور بطلان نکاح کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے شہادت کاملی یعنی شہادت شاہدین ضروری ہے۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ دو مرد گواہی دیں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں۔ اس کے برخلاف گوشت کیونکہ کسی چیز کے کھانے کی حرمت زوالِ ملک سے جدا ہو سکتی ہے۔ یعنی یہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ ایک چیز کا کھانا حرام ہو لیکن اس کی ملک زائل نہ ہو۔ بلکہ باقی رہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ حرمت تناول اور ملک دونوں جمع ہو سکتے ہیں۔ مثلاً ایک کافر شراب کا مالک ہے۔ پھر یہ کافر مسلمان ہو گیا تو اس مسلمان کیلئے اس شراب کا پینا حرام ہے حالانکہ اس کی ملک باقی ہے اس طرح ایک شخص مٹی کا مالک ہے تو اس شخص کیلئے مٹی کا کھانا حرام ہے اور ملک اس کی باقی ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی یہ گوشت مشتری کیلئے حرام ہے لیکن اس کی ملک زائل نہیں ہوئی تو اس صورت میں شہادت صرف گوشت کی حرمت پر ہوئی نہ کہ زوال ملک پر اور حرمت امر دینی ہے اور سابق میں معلوم ہو چکا کہ امر دینی کیلئے ایک آدمی کی شہادت کافی ہے۔ اسلئے ایک آدمی کی خبر سے یہ گوشت حرام ہو گیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
And testimony of women alone is not accepted in fosterage; rather it is established by testimony of two men, or a man and two women. Malik said: it is established by testimony of one woman if she is described as just, because prohibition is a right of the sacred law, so it is established by a single report, like one who buys meat and a single person informs him that it is the slaughter of a Magian. For us: the establishment of prohibition does not admit separation from dissolution of ownership in the chapter of marriage, and dissolution of ownership is not established except by testimony of two men or a man and two women, unlike meat, because the prohibition of consumption is separable from dissolution of ownership, so it is considered a religious matter, and Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is what persons' testimony is necessary to prove fosterage. There is disagreement. The Hanafi school: fosterage is proven by testimony of two men or one man and two women; testimony of women alone is insufficient. Shafi'i says: testimony of four women is accepted in fosterage. Malik said: one woman's testimony establishes fosterage provided she is just. Shafi'i's proof: Fosterage relates to the woman's breast, and looking at the breast is forbidden, so men cannot have knowledge of it. For matters men cannot know, according to Shafi'i, four women's testimony is required so that two women take the place of one man. Reply: Fosterage is not among things men cannot know; in fact men can know it—for example, close relatives (dhawi al-arham) may look at her breast. So this proof is unacceptable. Malik's proof: Prohibition is a right of the sacred law, and rights of the sacred law are religious matters. So prohibition is a religious matter, and a religious matter is established by one person's testimony (whether man or woman, provided just). Example: a man buys meat, then one person informs the buyer that it is the slaughter of a fire-worshipper, then the meat becomes forbidden to that buyer; he cannot eat it nor feed others. Thus, for establishing religious matters, one person's testimony suffices. Our proof: In marriage, establishment of prohibition is inseparable from dissolution of ownership. It cannot be that prohibition of marriage is established by fosterage while the ownership of marriage remains, because with permanent prohibition continuance of marriage is impossible. So when prohibition is established by fosterage, the marriage becomes void. And to prove voidness of marriage, complete testimony—i.e., testimony of two witnesses—is necessary. Therefore we say: two men should testify or one man and two women. Contrary to meat, because the prohibition of eating can be separated from dissolution of ownership. That is, it is possible that eating something is forbidden but ownership of it is not dissolved; rather it remains. In short, prohibition of consumption and ownership can coexist. For example, a disbeliever owns wine; then he becomes Muslim, so wine is forbidden to him while his ownership remains. Similarly, a man owns soil; eating soil is forbidden while ownership remains. Likewise, this meat is forbidden to the buyer, but his ownership is not dissolved. So here testimony is only about the prohibition of meat, not about dissolution of ownership. And prohibition is a religious matter, and it is known that for a religious matter one person's testimony suffices. Therefore by one person's information the meat becomes forbidden. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number and gender of witnesses required to prove fosterage (rada'). The text begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: women alone cannot testify to establish fosterage; rather, it requires two men or one man and two women. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position. It then reports Imam Malik's view that one just woman suffices, and explains his reasoning: fosterage establishes a prohibition (hurma) which is a right of the sacred law, and such rights are religious matters that can be proven by a single report. He analogizes to meat: if one trustworthy person informs a buyer that the meat is from an unlawful slaughter, the buyer must refrain. The Hanafi response refutes this by distinguishing between the prohibition (hurma) in fosterage and in meat. In fosterage, the prohibition is permanent and inseverable from the dissolution of ownership (i.e., marriage). Since proving the dissolution of marriage (which results from fosterage) requires two men or one man and two women, the same standard applies to proving fosterage. In contrast, the prohibition of meat can coexist with ownership; thus a single report is sufficient for the religious aspect, but ownership remains intact. The commentary also addresses Imam Shafi'i's view (four women) and rebuts it, noting that fosterage is not exclusively private; men like close relatives can witness it. Thus the Hanafi position remains the mufta bihi (relied-upon ruling).

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage: the suckling relationship that establishes certain marriage prohibitions.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court; the act of bearing witness.
حرمة (hurma): Prohibition, specifically the marital prohibition created by fosterage.
زوال الملك (zawal al-milk): Dissolution of ownership; in this context, termination of the marriage contract.
امر ديني (amr dini): A religious matter; a right of the sacred law that can be established by lesser evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what testimony establishes fosterage (rada')?
A) Two men or one man and two women.
B) One man or one woman.
C) Four women.
D) One woman if she is just.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires two men or one man and two women to prove fosterage, because the prohibition is inseparable from marriage dissolution, demanding complete testimony.
